- **Why:** durable record of the autonomous Print Translator evaluation that surfaced (and quantified) the classifier-gate defect fixed in v3.128.3.
- **What:** `docs/eval/print-translator-campaign/` — 25-print official-OEM `corpus_manifest`, `results/` (11 real handler runs + 10 gate-bypassed real-prompt/real-cascade/real-image explanations, OCR-empty on the dev box and caveated throughout), `review_worksheet.csv` (technician-judgment columns blank), `RANKED_REPORT.md`, `GAPS.md`, `rejected.md`, `LIVE_TELEGRAM_RUNBOOK.md`, `regression_fixtures/` (xfail, not CI-collected), `images/MANIFEST.md` (hashes + source URLs). Runner: `tools/print_translator_eval/`.
- **Copyright:** the downloaded single-page OEM schematic PNGs are kept **local and git-ignored** (`images/*.png`) — only metadata (hashes + URLs) is committed. Eval artifacts only; no production/prompt/wiring change.

### v3.128.3 (2026-07-10) - fix(vision): print-classifier gate — real electrical prints stop mis-routing to EQUIPMENT_PHOTO
- **Why:** the autonomous Print Translator campaign (`docs/eval/print-translator-campaign/RANKED_REPORT.md`) measured, on real official-OEM prints with real inference, that `VisionWorker._classify_photo` mis-classified **10/11 (91%)** to `EQUIPMENT_PHOTO`/`NAMEPLATE` — the vision model correctly described each as a drawing, but two deterministic defects blocked the Print Translator (and the whole ELECTRICAL_PRINT path) from ever triggering.
- **What:** two surgical fixes to `mira-bots/shared/workers/vision_worker.py::_classify_photo`:
  - **Precedence:** new `STRONG_PRINT_SIGNALS` set ("wiring diagram", "schematic", "ladder logic", "one-line diagram", "connection diagram", "electrical drawing", …) checked **after** the nameplate checks but **before** the equipment-face keywords — a described drawing is a drawing regardless of which equipment it depicts, so "wiring diagram of a VFD **drive**" no longer loses to the word "drive".
  - **Word-boundary matching:** new `_kw_in` helper (`(?<!\w)…(?!\w)`, cached) replaces substring matching for the equipment/print/nameplate keyword sets, so "led" no longer matches inside "ti**led**", "drive" not inside "**drive**r", "run" not inside "**run**way". NAMEPLATE_OCR_FIELDS keeps substring matching on purpose (units like "5HP"/"60Hz" abut digits).
- **Impact:** the real electrical prints the campaign submitted now reach the translator; genuine equipment faceplate + nameplate photos are unchanged (guarded by tests). No prompt, wiring-DB, or architecture change.
- **Tests:** `+12` `mira-bots/tests/test_vision_classify_print_gate.py` — pins the fix against the exact real vision-model strings captured in the campaign (GS20 "wiring diagram … drive", the "titled" substring case, ABB ACS355 "connection diagram") now → `ELECTRICAL_PRINT`, plus word-boundary cases and over-correction guards (real faceplate stays `EQUIPMENT_PHOTO`, nameplate stays `NAMEPLATE`). 231 classification-adjacent tests still pass. Staging-only, no prod deploy.

### v3.128.2 (2026-07-10) - fix(bot): lazy-load the tools/ wiring writer — stop mira-bot-telegram crash-loop
- **Incident:** rebuilding the telegram bot image (deploy #2603) surfaced a latent crash: `bot.py` -> `from shared import wiring_intake` -> `shared/wiring_intake.py` did an **eager top-level** `import wiring_schematic_import` (a `tools/` writer). The bot image ships `shared/` but not `tools/` (and the path math resolves to `/tools` in the flattened container), so every start died `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'wiring_schematic_import'` -> `Restarting (1)` crash-loop. Pre-existing bug from the wiring PRs, surfaced by the rebuild.
- **Fix:** make the `tools/` writer import **lazy** — `_load_schematic()` imports it on first *use* (writer/intake path only), so `import wiring_intake` and the reader Q&A path always work regardless of whether `tools/` is present. No behavior change where `tools/` is available (writer path unchanged); images without `tools/` now start cleanly instead of crash-looping.
- **Tests:** `mira-bots/tests/test_wiring_intake.py` (39) + `tests/test_wiring_schematic_import.py` (10) pass; verified `import shared.wiring_intake` succeeds with `tools/` absent from `sys.path` (the container condition).

### v3.128.1 (2026-07-10) - fix(ops): ship container ops-agents into the bot image + create the 2 missing runners
- **Why:** all three container ops-agents (`morning_brief`, `safety_alert`, `pm_escalation`) failed **every** cron run — two pre-existing breakages unrelated to the alert-routing work (#2558/#2575 only added `-e TELEGRAM_ALERT_*` to already-broken commands): (1) `mira-bots/telegram/Dockerfile` never COPYed `mira-bots/agents/` → `/app/agents/*_runner.py` = "No such file"; (2) only `morning_brief_runner.py` ever existed — `pm_escalation_runner.py` and `safety_alert_runner.py` were referenced by cron but absent.
- **What:** `Dockerfile` now `COPY mira-bots/agents/ ./agents/` (ships all three runners; they import from `/app/shared`, already present). New `pm_escalation_runner.py` (due/overdue PMs from `pm_schedules` via `shared.pm_scheduler.get_due_pms`; flags `critical`; invents nothing) and `safety_alert_runner.py` (safety-intent / `SAFETY_ALERT` turns from local `mira.db` `interactions` over 24h; concise all-clear when none). Both send **only** to the ops alert bot (`TELEGRAM_ALERT_*` → staging, same precedence as `morning_brief`), never `@FactoryLM_Diagnose`; both fail-soft.
- **Tests:** `tests/test_ops_agent_runners.py` (9 cases) — PM message building, safety digest, all-clear paths, alert-channel precedence. Staging-only; `install_crons.sh` re-installs the crontab on deploy so the three agents run for real.

### v3.128.0 (2026-07-09) - feat(telegram): Print Translator — print photo → plain-English theory of operation (read-only, grounded)
- **Why:** the wiring lane (PR-1..4) writes/reads structured connections; the lighter, higher-immediacy value for a tech is *understanding* a print. Print Translator lets a technician send a photo of an electrical print with "explain this / theory of operation" and get a senior-tech plain-English explanation — grounded ONLY in the visible print, with **no wiring-DB expansion, no new tables/migrations/Hub flow, no writes of any kind**.
- **What:** new pure module `mira-bots/shared/print_translator.py` + one additive, fall-through fast-path `_try_print_translator_reply` in `mira-bots/telegram/bot.py`. Reuses the existing vision classifier (`engine.vision`) + inference cascade (`engine.router`) + the multimodal message shape from `_analyze_schematic_with_question` — **no `engine.py` edits.**
  - **Trigger:** print-explanation caption (`is_theory_request`) AND `vision_data["classification"]=="ELECTRICAL_PRINT"`. Cheap intent reject first (no vision call for non-theory captions).
  - **Grounding:** feeds `ocr_items` verbatim + the image; `THEORY_SYSTEM_PROMPT` forbids inventing wire numbers/terminals/device tags, requires flagging unreadable items, and uses hedged framing ("According to this print…", "This appears to show…") — never claims the installed machine is actually wired that way.
  - **Output:** exact 6 sections — *What this appears to be · Main visible components · Plain-English theory of operation · What must be true for it to work · What would stop it from working · Unclear or unreadable items.*
  - **Fall-through / precedence:** ordered nameplate → wiring-intake → **print-translator** → generic; returns `False` (untouched) for non-print photos, non-theory captions, and the nameplate/drive + wiring flows. Graceful `FALLBACK_REPLY` on LLM failure (empty return **or** a raised malformed-provider exception — both degrade, never crash).
- **Doctrine:** read-only generation — **no `wiring_connections` writes, no proposed rows, no control/PLC writes, no graph ingestion.** It persists nothing.
- **Tests:** `+43` hermetic `mira-bots/tests/test_print_translator.py` + `test_telegram_print_translator.py` (vision + router mocked): intent detection, 6-section prompt, OCR-verbatim grounding / no invented labels, trigger, non-print + non-theory fall-through, nameplate/wiring unchanged, no-writes assertions, and LLM-failure fallback (return-empty **and** raised-exception, the latter from an adversarial implementation-review finding). Auto-collected by `pytest mira-bots/tests/`. No migration, no Hub change; staging-only, no prod deploy.

### v3.127.0 (2026-07-09) - feat(telegram): wiring loop — photo → proposed rows, text → verified-only cited Q&A (PR-4)
- **Why:** PR-1/PR-2 gave `wiring_connections` writers, PR-3 gave it a reader/scorecard/Q&A — the missing product loop was the phone. This turns a Telegram wiring-diagram photo into `proposed` rows and lets a technician ask wiring questions answered ONLY from verified evidence, on the surface a maintenance tech actually uses.
- **What:** new `mira-bots/shared/wiring_intake.py` (pure logic + thin DB glue) + two additive, fall-through fast-paths in `mira-bots/telegram/bot.py` — reusing every merged seam, no parallel path:
  - **Photo intake** (caption "CV-101 add this wiring"): reuses `engine._extract_schematic` (PR-2, unedited) → `wiring_schematic_import.kg_payload_to_rows` → `write_rows` → `approval_state='proposed'` rows tagged `proposed_by='telegram:wiring_intake'`. Replies a preview (component/connection counts, sample wires, "PROPOSED — not trusted" warning). Never auto-verifies.
  - **Text Q&A** ("Where does W200 land?", "CV-101 what does W200 land on?"): reuses `wiring_profile.load_profile` + `answer_wiring_question` (PR-3, unedited) — answers ONLY from `verified` rows with ≥1 citation + a `read_only=true, fallback_used=false` footer; refuses proposed-only ("needs approval"), honest "no record" when absent; **no generic LLM fallback**.
  - **Asset scoping:** if no asset is named, MIRA asks for it and writes/reads nothing — never guesses an asset. (Per-chat asset memory deliberately deferred — no reusable table without a migration; asset comes from the message.)
- **mig-026 doctrine decision (recorded, not silent):** LLM/vision-derived rows **direct-INSERT as `proposed`** via the reused PR-2 seam, NOT `ai_suggestions` — because `ai_suggestions` has no wiring `suggestion_type`, `proposal_writer` is `kg_edge`-only, and Hub `/proposals` has no wiring approve path, so Option B is a large multi-surface build, not the smallest doctrine-consistent path. Human gate preserved (proposed + reader trusts verified-only). Follow-up issue tracks the ai_suggestions/Hub-review bridge.
- **Tests:** `+52` hermetic `mira-bots/tests/test_wiring_intake.py` + `test_telegram_wiring_hooks.py` (+ `fixtures/wiring_intake/`) — intent parsing, payload→proposed rows (controls dropped), fake-cursor RLS+idempotent write, preview, verified-cited / proposed-refusal / no-record answer formatting, and Telegram routing (intake, ask-if-no-asset writes nothing, fall-through for non-wiring, no generic fallback). Includes a regression test for the asset-prefixed-question fix (asset stripped so the wire isn't mis-read as a terminal). Auto-collected by `pytest mira-bots/tests/`. No `engine.py`/`tools/`/`wiring_profile/` edits, no migration, no Hub change; staging-only, no prod deploy.
### v3.126.1 (2026-07-09) - fix(ci): make main green — Architecture Check + Eval Offline root-cause fixes
- **Why:** the two checks were red on `main` for days, jamming clean-PR signal. Root-caused all three underlying failures (not papered over).
- **Architecture Check pytest** (`test_crawler_cannot_import_bots`): `mira-crawler/tasks/eval_scorer.py` (added #2576) **statically** imported `from shared.inference.router import InferenceRouter`, coupling the crawler to the bots/shared inference cascade the layering rule forbids. Fix: resolve the router **dynamically** (`importlib.import_module`) inside the existing fail-open `try` — the scorer's router need is an *optional runtime* dependency (drive-pack rows score deterministically without it), not a static coupling. Behavior unchanged; `mira-crawler/tests/test_eval_scorer.py` 10/10 still pass.
- **Architecture Check env-drift** (the same job also runs `tools/check_env_drift.py`): `HUB_BASE_PATH` (default `/hub`) and `HUB_INGEST_TOKEN` (Telegram→Hub `/api/uploads/folder` intake, #2547) were used in compose but undocumented → 2-offender drift gate. Fix: document both in `docs/env-vars.md`; drift check now reports "OK: no uncovered env-var drift."
- **Eval Offline** (`tests/lead_hunter/test_celery_tasks.py::test_discovery_{msca,ddg}_*`): the lead-hunter tests `import discover`/`celery_tasks`/`hunt` as **bare top-level names** that collide with same-named modules in the monorepo (`mira-crawler/tasks/discover.py`, `tests/eval/celery_tasks.py`). Under the full `pytest tests/ -n auto` run, another test mutates `sys.path`/`sys.modules` first, so bare `import discover` resolved to mira-crawler's copy → `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'celery'/'mira_crawler'`. A one-time `sys.path.insert` at conftest import time wasn't robust to that runtime mutation. Fix: `tests/lead_hunter/conftest.py` now has an **autouse fixture** that pins `tools/lead-hunter` at `sys.path[0]` and shadow-evicts colliding modules per-test, restoring the wider suite's import state after. Verified with a faithful red→green repro of the exact CI traceback.
- **Scope:** two code files (`eval_scorer.py`, `conftest.py`) + docs (`env-vars.md`) + VERSION/CHANGELOG. No production-code behavior change; all three are test-harness/layering/doc hygiene.

### v3.126.0 (2026-07-09) - feat(wiring): machine wiring profile + trust scorecard + citable Q&A + eval pack (read-only lane over wiring_connections)
- **Why:** PR-1/PR-2 gave `wiring_connections` its first *writers* (cited YAML + schematic extractor → `proposed` rows) but the table had no *reader*. This builds the product lane that turns those rows into trustworthy maintenance intelligence — strengthening the evidence loop (proof, never guess, read-only, human-approval-before-trust), never loosening it.
- **What:** new read-only package `mira-bots/shared/wiring_profile/` — four modules, all reading the ONE `wiring_connections` table (no second architecture, no new writer, no schema change; the reader scopes an asset via the existing `evidence_summary->>'asset'`):
  - `schema.py` — `WiringConnection` / `MachineWiringProfile`. **Only `approval_state='verified'` is trusted**; `trusted()`==`approved` is the only set an answer is built from; `find_by_wire` is exact-normalized (`"200"` ≠ `"W200"` — false-positive guard).
  - `reader.py` — `profile_from_rows` (pure) + `load_profile` (SELECT-only, RLS via `set_config`, `psycopg2` local-import). Never coerces: absent optional fields stay `None`, `function_class='unknown'` stays `'unknown'`, `evidence_summary` round-trips verbatim.
  - `scorecard.py` — `score_profile` → `WiringTrustScore`, mirroring the drive-pack scorecard gate-dict + trust ladder (`no_wiring`→`proposed_only`→`partial`→`trusted`). Gates: has_wiring, has_approved (not proposed-only), approved_all_sourced, approved_human_readable, approved_field_confirmed. Deliberately NOT wired into a repo-wide CI gate over live data (CV-101 is all-`proposed` by design and MUST score `proposed_only`).
  - `ask.py` — `answer_wiring_question` → `WiringAnswer`, mirroring the `DrivePackAnswer` contract. Answers "Where does W200 land?" / "What is connected to I-00?" from **approved rows only**, ≥1 citation each; REFUSES with "not enough APPROVED evidence" when a match exists only in `proposed`/`needs_review`; honest "no record" when absent. Never invents an endpoint/wire/terminal; `read_only=True`, `fallback_used=False` always.
- **Doctrine:** trusted == verified-only; a `wiring_connections`-sourced answer always carries a citation, a refusal always carries none; unknown stays unknown; no control writes; reuses the existing writers (`tools/wiring_map_import.py`, `tools/wiring_schematic_import.py`) untouched.
- **Tests:** `+74` `mira-bots/tests/test_wiring_profile_{reader,scorecard,ask}.py` (+ `fixtures/wiring_profile/`) — six hermetic suites: approval enforcement, provenance preservation, unknown-field, false-positive (W200≠200, absent→no-record), citation-or-refuse, scorecard ladder. Auto-collected by the existing `pytest mira-bots/tests/` CI step under `--cov=mira-bots/shared` (no new CI step). No migration; staging-only, no prod deploy.

No new migration; no second table; no Drive-Pack schema change; no `schema_version` bump.

### v3.123.0 (2026-07-09) - feat(eval): relational distillation — grounded KG edges from real Q&A (flywheel Phase 4b)
- **Why:** Phases 3b/4a distil coverage gaps and golden cases from captured turns; the relational half was still spec'd-but-unbuilt. A *matched* drive-pack **fault** turn is grounded-by-construction (cited, `fallback_used=False`) — real evidence that a drive family has a documented failure mode. This closes the loop by turning those turns into reviewable knowledge-graph edges.

- **Never auto-verified (Iron Rule).** The only path to a verified `kg_relationships` row is a human decide on `/api/proposals/[id]/decide` (ADR-0017, `managing-the-knowledge-graph`). Unmatched turns stay Phase-3b gaps; parameter/engine turns yield nothing (no-guess). `RESOLVED_BY`-from-corrections needs a fuzzy step and is a deliberate future extension.
- **Writer:** additive optional `evidence_type` param on `propose_relationship` / `propose_relationship_cursor` (default `oem_kb` — unchanged for all existing callers) so a conversation-sourced edge cites `technician_note` truthfully.
- **Benchmark:** extended `tools/flywheel_benchmark.py` to a **6th criterion** ("Relational distillation") + rubric; the offline fixture still scores **100%** and the grader is proven to FAIL on a wrong-edge stage.

### v3.121.1 (2026-07-09) - chore(infra): baseline staging migration ledger to zero drift + hard-gate (W3 follow-up)
- **Why:** W3 (v3.121.0) shipped the ingest apply path + drift guard but the guard was **warn-only** because staging's `schema_migrations` ledger was 22 behind. This closes the foundation: staging is baselined to **zero drift** and the staging drift check is now a **hard gate** — so migration drift can't be silently ignored before Phase 4b adds `relationship_proposals` tables.
- **Staging baseline (verify-then-record, no blind marking):** each of the 21 remaining drifting migrations was classified by probing staging's **actual** schema (the table/column/constraint it creates). **17** whose DDL was already present were recorded via `seed-ledger` (no SQL re-run); **4** were `apply`d after verifying prerequisites + idempotency — `059_namespace_filing_cabinet` (the one genuinely-missing column `namespace_direct_uploads.makes`), plus `053` (scoped no-op DELETE), `058` (DROP+CREATE POLICY), `061` (GRANT). Result: `migration_drift.py` → **82/82 recorded, 0 drift**.
- **Hard gate:** `migration-drift-check.yml` now fails loud for **staging** (zero-drift baseline established); **prod stays warn-only** (its ledger isn't baselined — needs the approved `production`-gated path; no prod psql from a code session). Also made the drift tool's summary ASCII-clean (was an em-dash that mojibaked on Windows).
- **Runbook:** `docs/runbooks/migration-apply-and-drift.md` updated with the completed baseline (exact 17+4 reconciliation), the staging hard-gate state, and the prod-baseline follow-up.
- **Prod follow-up (owner: human/DBA):** baseline the prod ledger the same way via the approved path, then drop `--warn-only` for prod to make it a hard gate too.

### v3.121.0 (2026-07-09) - feat(infra): mira-ingest migration automation + drift detection (W3)
- **Why (root cause):** the flywheel's mig 013 (`conversation_eval.meta`) reached prod via a one-off manual script but **never staging** — `apply-ingest-migrations.yml` was **prod-only and ledger-less**, so nothing could apply ingest migrations to staging and nothing detected the gap. That silent drift is why the `--live` benchmark crashed on staging. This is the durable fix so migrations can't silently diverge across dev/staging/prod again.
- **Apply path:** `apply-ingest-migrations.yml` rewritten to mirror the Hub workflow — a `target` (staging | prod) input, a `schema_migrations` **ledger** (records each applied file; `migrations=all` auto-skips already-applied), a `seed-ledger` mode to baseline an existing DB, and a generic post-apply ledger report (was hardcoded to the 006 tsvector probe). Keeps the `-- Block 1/2` `CONCURRENTLY` split.
- **Drift guard:** `tools/migration_drift.py` compares every repo migration (both `mira-hub` + `mira-ingest` dirs) to a DB's `schema_migrations` ledger and fails (or `--warn-only` reports) on anything missing. `migration-drift-check.yml` runs it warn-only against staging daily + on demand (read-only — safe against prod). Ships warn-only until the ledgers are baselined; flip to hard-gate per the runbook.
- **Proven on staging:** the drift detector found **22** missing migrations on staging (incl. `013` and all 11 ingest migrations); applying + recording `013` via the ledger path dropped drift to 21 and cleared 013 (61/82 recorded). The apply→ledger→drift loop works end-to-end.
- **Runbook:** `docs/runbooks/migration-apply-and-drift.md` — apply order, the three modes, drift detection, the one-time ledger-baseline procedure, and the Windows `channel_binding` note. Prevents this from being a one-off manual fix.
- **Tests:** `+8` in `tests/test_migration_drift.py` (pure `find_drift`/`repo_migrations`/`render`; guards that `013_conversation_eval_meta.sql` is discoverable) — named in the CI "Unit Tests" job.

### v3.120.4 (2026-07-09) - fix(eval): gap report groups under the parameter, not the model name
- **Why:** seeding the P01.24 scenario into **staging** and running the real pipeline surfaced a grouping weakness. The gap report keyed each gap on the *first* token in the question, and a model name like `GS10` also matches the parameter-token regex — so `"GS10 P01.24 meaning?"` grouped under a phantom **`GS10`** bucket instead of `P01.24`, fragmenting the count (P01.24 showed 3 asks, not 4). Real technician traffic constantly leads with the model, so this would fragment real reports.
- **Fix:** `gap_report.grouping_token(tokens)` — prefer a **dotted parameter id** (`P01.24`) as the grouping key when present, falling back to the first token otherwise (bare fault codes like `CE10` are unaffected). `aggregate_gaps` now uses it. Verified on the real staging DB: model-led and parameter-led asks consolidate into one `P01.24 = 4` bucket, no phantom `GS10`.
- **Tests:** `+3` in `tools/drive-pack-extract/tests/test_gap_report.py` (dotted-preference both orderings, fallback for bare/empty, model-led + param-led consolidate into one bucket).

### v3.120.1 (2026-07-08) - fix(eval): flywheel tools fail-clean when capture schema is absent
- **Why:** the first `flywheel_benchmark.py --live` run against **staging** surfaced two real weaknesses. (1) Migration 013 (`conversation_eval.meta`) had reached prod (manual script) but **never staging** — apply-migrations.yml is Hub-only and doesn't cover `mira-ingest` migrations. Applied 013 to staging out-of-band (additive/idempotent), so `--live` now runs there. (2) With `meta` absent, every flywheel tool crashed with a raw `psycopg2 UndefinedColumn` traceback.
- **Fix:** `gap_report.capture_schema_ready(cur)` + `META_MISSING_MSG` — the DB-glue `main()`s of `gap_report.py`, `gap_suggestion.py`, and `flywheel_benchmark.py --live` now check for the `meta` column first and exit `3` with an **actionable** message ("apply migration 013 to this environment") instead of a traceback. Also added a best-effort `sys.stdout.reconfigure("utf-8")` to the tool `main()`s so the em-dash/`…`/`×` in summaries don't mojibake on a Windows cp1252 console.
- **Tests:** `+3` in `tools/drive-pack-extract/tests/test_gap_report.py` (fake-cursor `capture_schema_ready` true/false + the message is actionable). Verified live: `--live`, `gap_report`, `gap_suggestion --dry-run`, and `harvest` all run clean against staging after the fix.
- **Known follow-up (W3):** `mira-ingest` migrations still have **no automated apply path** (only Hub migrations are covered by `apply-migrations.yml`). That's the root cause of the staging drift; a workflow fix to cover `mira-ingest` migrations is the durable remedy (not in this PR).

### v3.120.0 (2026-07-08) - feat(eval): flywheel benchmark + grading rubric (proof the loop works)
- **Why:** Each phase shipped unit tests, but "tests pass" ≠ "the loop works end-to-end." This is the proof: a grading rubric + a benchmark that runs the **real** stage cores over one ground-truth scenario and scores how faithfully the flywheel distils it. Deterministic + CI-gated — a regression in any stage drops the score and fails the build.
- **Rubric:** `docs/specs/flywheel-benchmark-rubric.md` — 5 criteria (0–100 each, PASS ≥ 90): capture→label accuracy, gap surfacing, distill precision, no-fabrication/no-guess integrity, gate safety. The scenario is the real one that motivated the flywheel (technicians repeatedly ask GS10 **P01.24**, undocumented) plus grounded turns, other packs, an unregistered pack, engine turns, and human-corrected turns.
- **Harness:** `tools/flywheel_benchmark.py` grades the real cores — `eval_scorer.label_drive_pack_row` (Phase 2), `gap_report.aggregate_gaps` (3a), `gap_suggestion.build_gap_suggestions` (3b), `harvest_golden_cases.row_to_proposal` (4a). Offline mode prints the scored table and exits non-zero on FAIL (`--json` for machine output). `--live` (read-only, ungraded) reports throughput over real staging `conversation_eval`: turns captured, matched vs gap, top gaps, packs that would get a suggestion, harvest candidates waiting. **Current offline score: 100% PASS (24/24 decisions).**
- **Falsifiable:** `tests/test_flywheel_benchmark.py` asserts the healthy fixture scores 100 AND that each grader **fails** on a deliberately broken stage (mislabel, misrank, unregistered-pack suggestion, non-review-only/pre-accepted suggestion, phantom gap) — so a green 100 is meaningful, not vacuous. Two new CI steps in "Unit Tests": the falsifiability tests (gate) + a visible scorecard.
- **Scope:** proves the distillation *plumbing* generates the right reviewable artifacts. It does **no** model training and does not replace the human `proposed → verified` / real-manual-trust gates (`feedback_extractor_real_manual_trust_gate`) — those still apply.

### v3.119.0 (2026-07-08) - feat(eval): golden-case harvester (distillation flywheel, Phase 4a)
- **Why:** Phases 1–3 capture, score, and report drive-pack gaps. Phase 4a closes the production→test loop from `docs/specs/bot-eval-loop-spec.md` (§ "Golden-case harvester"): every reply Mike confirmed **bad** with a `correction` becomes a permanent regression case so the same mistake can't ship again. `.claude/plans/use-avail-skills-to-functional-wave.md` Phase 4.
- **Tool:** new `tools/harvest_golden_cases.py` — reads `conversation_eval WHERE human_verdict='bad' AND correction IS NOT NULL AND golden_case_added=false` (uses the mig-012 `idx_..._harvest` index) and prints paste-ready `tests/bot_regression.py` `GOLDEN_CASES` dicts (`name`/`input`/`intent`) with the correction, the bad response, and the source-row UUID as **review comments**. Run: `NEON_DATABASE_URL=… python tools/harvest_golden_cases.py [--limit N]`.
- **Print-only, human-gated — never auto-promotes.** It NEVER edits `tests/bot_regression.py`; "golden cases are forever, a human eyeball is the gate" (spec § 191–210). Its only write is the gated `--mark-applied --ids <uuid…>` pass that flips `golden_case_added=true` after Mike commits the cases (so a row is harvested at most once).
- **Spec reconciliation:** the spec sketched an `expected_substring_in_response` field, but the shipped `bot_regression.py` suite is **offline/no-LLM** (checks intent + clarification, not response text). So a harvested case emits the runnable `name`/`input`/`intent` (the intent tier checks it) plus the correction as a reviewer comment — honest to what CI actually runs. Target is `bot_regression.py` (per the spec + mig-012's own comment), not the RAGAS `golden_factorylm.csv` the plan loosely named (that column set needs retrieved `contexts`, which `conversation_eval` doesn't store).
- **Tests:** `tests/test_harvest_golden_cases.py` (+11: slugify caps/fallback, field mapping + intent default, paste-ready render + review comments, quote-escaping via `repr`, correction truncation, empty-queue message, batch footer carries all ids + the exact `--mark-applied` command, name uniqueness). Named explicitly in the CI "Unit Tests" job (root `tests/` is not collected wholesale there). Pure core; no DB in tests.

### v3.118.0 (2026-07-08) - feat(eval): drive-pack gap → review suggestion (distillation flywheel, Phase 3b)
- **Why:** Phase 3a (v3.117.0) reports which parameter/fault tokens technicians keep asking that a pack can't answer. Phase 3b closes the loop by turning a *recurring* gap into a Hub review item, so the worklist reaches the review queue instead of a file. `.claude/plans/use-avail-skills-to-functional-wave.md` Phase 3.
- **Tool:** new `tools/drive-pack-extract/gap_suggestion.py` — reads the same unmatched drive-pack turns from `conversation_eval` (reuses `gap_report.aggregate_gaps`), resolves each *registered* pack's `registry_manual_id` from `registry/sources.json`, and for packs over `--min-gap-count` writes a **review-only** `drive_pack_update` `ai_suggestions` row (`status='pending'`). Run: `NEON_DATABASE_URL=… python tools/drive-pack-extract/gap_suggestion.py --tenant-id <uuid> [--min-gap-count 3] [--dry-run]`.
- **Reuses the existing gate end-to-end — no Hub change, no migration.** The row carries `registry_manual_id`, so accepting it drives the existing `suggestion-accept.ts` → `drain_build_requests.py` → `update_candidate.py` re-extraction into a *staged candidate* (guarded by `assert_not_live_packs`). If the PDF isn't cached, the drain records `build_status='failed'` with a "supply the manual" reason and a human runs `update_candidate.py` by hand. **Never auto-promoted** (ADR-0025, `.claude/rules/train-before-deploy.md`).
- **Distinct from the kb-growth bridge:** that raises a `drive_pack_update` on a manual *hash change*; this raises one on a *question-driven coverage gap*. Deduped independently by `extracted_data->>'source'='gap_report'` (one pending row per pack). Tenant-scoped via `set_config('app.current_tenant_id', …)` (mirrors `proposal_writer.py`); `--dry-run` writes nothing.
- **Tests:** `tools/drive-pack-extract/tests/test_gap_suggestion.py` (+10: registry indexing, threshold + registered-only filtering, `registry_manual_id`/`source`/`review_only` contract, title/body worklist + by-hand command, token cap, multi-pack ranking, JSON round-trip, raw-rows→`aggregate_gaps`→build end-to-end) — auto-collected by the CI offline-tests job. Pure core; no DB in tests.

### v3.116.0 (2026-07-08) - feat(eval): auto-scorer/labeler for conversation_eval (distillation flywheel, Phase 2)
- **Why:** Phase 1 (v3.115.0) started capturing every drive-pack Q&A into `conversation_eval`; those rows had no signal yet. - **Guardrails:** fail-open end-to-end (no provider / unparseable judge / DB hiccup leaves the row unscored for a later retry, never raises into the worker); no migration (012 columns reused); no change to `engine.py`/`ask_api`/`drive_pack.py`/`ignition_chat.py`. Cross-package router import uses the established `mira-crawler`→`mira_bots.shared` path pattern.
- **Not in this PR (deploy step):** wiring the VPS Celery-beat schedule (`mira_eval.score_conversation_eval`, 03:00 UTC) — prod-touching, gated separately.
- **Tests:** `mira-bots/tests/test_eval_score_rubric.py` (+9: parse/clamp/fence-strip/mean-fallback/garbage) and `mira-crawler/tests/test_eval_scorer.py` (+10: deterministic matched/unmatched labels, mocked-router judge, fail-open on disabled/None/empty/unparseable, meta coercion) — added to the CI offline-tests job. 19 green; ruff check + format clean.

Every entry gets provenance: `source`, `family`, `trust_status`, `queue_reason`, `discovered_at`. - **Why:** live staging testing asked "what is P01.24?" as a follow-up. The continuity fix (v3.113.0) kept it in the GS10 conversation, but the pack documented only `P09.03` (+ 9 fault codes), so it honestly answered "not documented." This adds the real parameters so the follow-up gives a genuine, cited answer instead of a refusal.
- **What (all grounded, no fabrication):** added 7 P01 "Basic Parameters" to `packs/durapulse_gs10/pack.json` — `P01.00` (max operation frequency), `P01.01` (motor base frequency), `P01.02` (motor rated voltage), `P01.12` (accel time 1), `P01.13` (decel time 1), `P01.22` (JOG frequency), and **`P01.24` (S-curve for acceleration begin time 1)** — plus keypad view-cards for P01.12/P01.13/P01.24. Every field (name, range, default, unit, purpose) is transcribed from the **official DURApulse GS10 User Manual (1st Ed., Rev B)** chapter 4 (`cdn.automationdirect.com/static/manuals/gs10m/ch4.pdf`), each with a page citation (P01 summary p.4-8; details p.4-69/4-70; keypad procedure p.3-6).
- **Result:** "what is P01.24?" now returns `GS10 parameter P01.24 [S-curve for acceleration begin time 1]: …` with `[Source: … p.4-70]`, `matched=parameter`, `source: drive_pack`. Same for the other six. The **no-guess contract is intact** — a still-undocumented parameter (e.g. `P02.00`) still answers "not documented, here's what is covered," never a fabricated value.
- **Hub copy synced** byte-for-byte (`mira-hub/src/lib/drive-packs/gs10-pack.json`) per `test_drive_pack_hub_copy_sync`.
- **Tests:** `test_drive_packs.py` updated to assert P09.03 **and** P01.24 presence + that every parameter is `manual_cited` with a page (not an exact count, so future expansion won't break it); `test_telegram_drive_followup.py` updated — the reported P01.24 turn now asserts a real cited answer, and a new case pins the still-uncovered-parameter (P02.00) honest path. Drive-pack + telegram suite green (98).
- **Scope:** pack data + tests only. No resolver/engine/schema change; none of the protected files.

### v3.113.0 (2026-07-08) - feat(telegram): drive-conversation continuity — text follow-ups stay in the pack (un-gated)
- **Bug (staging):** after a nameplate photo correctly answered "what does CE10 mean?" for a GS10, the very next **text** turn ("what is P01.24?") returned the **invite-only enrollment wall** and had no memory of the GS10. Cause: the photo path answers *before* the enrollment gate (`shared/chat/dispatcher.py`), but a text turn goes straight through `handle_message → dispatcher.dispatch`, which gates unenrolled/non-admin users; and the fast path never remembered the resolved pack, so even past the gate the text turn didn't know it was about the GS10.
- **Fix — multi-turn continuity (the previously-deferred flow, now built):** a **bot-local** per-chat store `telegram_drive_context(chat_id, pack_id, updated_at)` — a **dedicated** SQLite table, separate from the engine's `conversation_state`, so there is **no `engine.py` change** (engine stays the reasoner, not a state bag). A nameplate/`/drive` identification writes it; a 30-min TTL keeps stale context from hijacking a new topic.
- **Text fast path:** `handle_message` now calls `_try_drive_pack_followup` **before** the engine dispatch. With a fresh drive context AND text that maps to the pack (or reads like a drive question — a parameter id `P09.03`, a fault code, or drive vocabulary), it answers from the pack: read-only, cited, **un-gated** (same public-OEM contract as the photo path — an unenrolled tester isn't dropped to the enrollment wall mid-conversation). General chat, FSM `yes`/`no` confirmations, and non-drive questions fall through **unchanged** to the normal gated dispatch.
- **No-guess preserved:** an undocumented parameter (P01.24 isn't in the GS10 pack yet — it carries P09.03 + 9 fault codes) gets the pack's honest "not documented, here's what is covered" answer, **never a fabricated value**. Expanding GS10 parameter coverage from the manual is separate, grounded content work (flagged, not done here).
- **Tests:** `mira-bots/tests/test_telegram_drive_followup.py` (+7): context round-trip + TTL; covered-parameter answered from pack; **the reported P01.24 case stays in-context + honest, not the invite wall**; non-drive text and bare `yes` fall through; no-context and stale-context fall through. Full drive/telegram suite green (35); ruff clean; Hub GS10 pack copy still synced.
- **Scope:** `bot.py` + one new test + doc/runbook updates. No change to `engine.py` / `ask_api` / `drive_pack.py` / `ignition_chat.py` / the dispatcher gate (general chat stays gated exactly as before).

### v3.112.0 (2026-07-08) - feat(drive-packs): Phase 2 — nameplate Asset Identity Packet + Manual Applicability (#2561)
- **What:** turns a nameplate scan into reusable, evidence-separated asset identity instead of using it only for one-shot answer routing (follow-on to #2560; issue #2561). Additive; the no-guess resolver is unchanged.
- **Raw OCR preserved** — `mira-bots/shared/workers/nameplate_worker.py::extract()` now returns `raw_text` (the verbatim, untruncated model response) on every path (success, JSON-parse-failure, and `None` on empty), alongside the existing 8 interpreted fields. Raw evidence is no longer discarded.
- **Asset Identity Packet** — new pure module `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/asset_identity.py`: `AssetIdentityPacket` (frozen dataclass keeping `raw_text` **separate** from interpreted fields) + `build_asset_identity(nameplate, raw_text, resolution, evidence_image_id)`. `sku_prefix` is derived only from the leading catalog token of `model_number` (`GS11N-20P2` → `GS11N`); never fabricated; `approval_status` starts `"unreviewed"` (a packet is a proposal). Pure, never raises.
- **Telegram fast path preserves evidence** — `bot.py::_try_nameplate_drive_pack_reply` now builds the packet from the extracted fields + resolution and audit-logs a concise identity summary instead of silently dropping the fields after routing. No reply/behavior change; still read-only, no LLM fallback, no engine/FSM touch. (Persisting the packet to a Hub review record is Phase 3.)
- **Manual Applicability Artifact** — new pure module `tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/applicability.py`: `ManualApplicability` + `applicability_from_source()` reshapes a manual-registry entry (`sources.json`, key `manuals`) into structured applicability, deriving `applies_to_catalog_prefixes` (e.g. GS11N/GS13N) while excluding series names (GS10/GS-10). Never fabricates.
- **Parity guard** — `mira-bots/tests/test_manual_applicability_parity.py` proves applicability survives source → pack: every `applicable_drive_models` entry for a live pack appears in that pack's `aliases`/`match_keywords` (verified for `durapulse_gs10` **and** `powerflex_525`). Data-layer invariant; NOT a runtime resolver change.
- **Design doc** `docs/drive-commander/phase2-asset-identity-and-applicability.md` (architecture, packet schema, applicability, trust rules; the Hub asset-candidate review record is **Phase 3 / design-only**).
- **Trust rules held:** manufacturer-only / ratings-only / ambiguous still refuse; serial identifies an asset but doesn't select a pack; catalog-backed aliases only (GS12N/GS14N stay excluded — not in the official GS10 spec).
- **Tests:** +16 (asset identity) +6 (raw_text) +5 (applicability parity); full drive-pack + nameplate suite green (85 + 6); ruff clean; Hub GS10 pack copy still byte-synced. Built with Haiku + Sonnet subagents on disjoint files; integration + doc-accuracy pass by the orchestrator.
- **Scope:** no change to `engine.py` / `ask_api` / `drive_pack.py` / `ignition_chat.py`; resolver unchanged.

### v3.129.5 (2026-07-11) - docs(plan): prod ingest storage fixes — embedder (Bravo Ollama down) + KG upsert ON CONFLICT
- **Discovery (issue #2562 Phase 1 OCR proof):** the OCR path works end-to-end (scanned PDF → Tika → 224 chars) but the chunk is **never stored / not citable**. Root cause is **not** OCR — it's the storage layer.
- **Primary:** prod embeddings go to Bravo's home-lab Ollama (`OLLAMA_BASE_URL=http://100.86.236.11:11434` in `factorylm/prd`), which is **offline** (`curl … :11434 → rc=7 connection refused`) → `0 chunks stored` for every manual (OCR *and* text-layer). `knowledge_entries.embedding` is `vector(768)` (nomic-embed-text), so any replacement must be 768-dim-compatible.
- **Secondary:** `kg_writer.py` `ON CONFLICT (tenant_id, entity_type, name)` errors "no matching constraint" despite a matching non-partial unique index (`kg_entities_tenant_type_name_key`) — anomalous; needs a staging repro. Blocks the KG write, not the citable chunk.
- **Plan doc:** `docs/plans/2026-07-08-prod-ingest-storage-fixes.md` — immediate unblock (restart Bravo Ollama), durable options (prod-resident Ollama container vs cloud 768-dim provider — **owner decision**), KG constraint-promotion fix, and the re-run verification. Plan only — no prod code change or deploy.

### v3.111.2 (2026-07-08) - fix(drive-packs): GS10 pack matches real nameplate catalog prefixes (GS11N/GS13N)
- **Bug the staging smoke found:** a real GS10-series drive photographed on the bench reads **MODEL: GS11N-20P2** — field nameplates print the *catalog part number*, never the series name "GS10". The `durapulse_gs10` pack's `family.aliases` / `nameplate.match_keywords` were only `["GS10","DURApulse","GS-10"]`, so `resolve_service_pack` correctly **refused to guess** (manufacturer recognized, no model match) — right behavior, but the pack data couldn't route a genuine GS10 drive. The resolver was NOT weakened; the data feeding it was completed.
- **Fix (grounded in official evidence, no fabrication):** add the GS10 series' catalog prefixes **`GS11N`** and **`GS13N`** to both `packs/durapulse_gs10/pack.json` (`aliases` + `match_keywords`) and the manual registry `tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/sources.json` (`applicable_drive_models`). Per AutomationDirect's GS10 spec (`cdn.automationdirect.com/static/specs/gs10drives.pdf`), the GS10 line has **exactly two** prefixes — `GS11N` (1-phase 120/230V) and `GS13N` (3-phase 230/460V). **`GS12N`/`GS14N`/600V do not exist in the GS10 line and were deliberately NOT added** (the strategy doc suggested them, but adding unverified SKUs would violate the no-guess/no-fabrication rule).
- **Result:** `GS11N-20P2` (and `GS13N-*`) now resolve to `durapulse_gs10`; a CE10 question returns the grounded, cited pack answer with footer `source: drive_pack · pack: durapulse_gs10 · fallback_used: false · read_only: true`.
- **No over-match:** GS11N/GS13N are unique to the GS10 line — the GS20 family (SKUs `GS21N`/`GS23N`) still does **not** match GS10 (invariant kept green). Manufacturer-only / ambiguous inputs still refuse.
- **Tests (`mira-bots/tests/test_service_pack_resolver.py`, +5):** GS11N-20P2 resolves; GS13N-43P0 resolves; GS11N end-to-end CE10 answer carries the footer fields; GS23N (GS20) still refuses; pack metadata carries GS11N/GS13N. Full drive-pack + nameplate suite green (63 passed); ruff clean; both JSON files validated.
- **Scope:** pack/registry data + tests only. No resolver/engine code change, no schema change, none of the protected files. The broader Nameplate-OCR / Manual-Applicability strategy (Asset Identity Packet, applicability-artifact schema, sources→pack propagation, Hub asset intake) is **phased as follow-up** — this ships only the immediate, grounded GS10 fix.

### v3.111.1 (2026-07-08) - fix(compose): Tika healthcheck uses a bash TCP probe (curl not in the image)
- **Bug (cosmetic false-unhealthy):** both `mira-tika` (`docker-compose.saas.yml`, prod `mira-tika-saas`) and `stg-mira-tika` (`docker-compose.staging-vps.yml`) used `test: ["CMD","curl","-f","http://localhost:9998/tika"]`, but the `apache/tika:3.1.0.0-full` image ships **no `curl`/`wget`** — so the internal healthcheck always failed and Docker reported `(unhealthy)` even though Tika was serving fine (proven repeatedly by an **external** `curl localhost:9998/tika` → "This is Tika Server (Apache Tika 3.1.0)"). Observed during the 2026-07-08 OCR activation.
- **Fix:** switch both to a dependency-free bash `/dev/tcp` port probe: `["CMD-SHELL", "timeout 5 bash -c '</dev/tcp/127.0.0.1/9998'"]`. The image is Ubuntu-based (`/bin/bash` present), so this succeeds when Tika is listening and needs no extra binary. Same `interval/timeout/retries/start_period`.
- **Scope/safety:** compose healthcheck test string only; no image, port, network, or service topology change; identical fix mirrored in prod + staging composes. Nothing `depends_on` Tika's health today, so this only removes the misleading `(unhealthy)` label.

### v3.110.2 (2026-07-08) - fix(staging): deploy-staging rebuilds mira-bot-telegram by default (stop bot image drift)
- **Bug (staging-only, deployment drift):** the staging Telegram smoke — nameplate photo + caption → Drive Commander pack answer (#2554) — returned **stale pre-#2554 behaviour** ("invite-only" + "Photo queued for knowledge base"). Root cause: `deploy-staging.yml`'s default `TARGETS` was `mira-pipeline mira-mcp mira-hub mira-web` — it **omitted `mira-bot-telegram`**. The build + `--force-recreate` steps are scoped to `$TARGETS`, and the full-stack `up -d` never rebuilds an existing image, so `stg-mira-bot-telegram` kept running a **2026-05-25 image** (verified via `docker image inspect`) even as newer commits deployed. The 2026-06-20 wording change (`d9b564b3`) and the 2026-07-07 fast path (`_try_nameplate_drive_pack_reply`, #2554) were never in the running staging container.
- **Fix:** add `mira-bot-telegram` to the default `TARGETS` so every staging deploy rebuilds it. **`mira-bot-slack` is deliberately NOT added** — staging runs no Slack bot (`docker-compose.staging-vps.yml` omits `SLACK_BOT_TOKEN` by design), so listing it would fail `docker compose build`.
- **Guard:** `tests/test_deploy_staging_targets.py` (+2) — (1) the default `TARGETS` must include `mira-bot-telegram`; (2) every default target must be a real service in `docker-compose.staging-vps.yml` (catches a phantom target like `mira-bot-slack` before deploy time). pytest+pyyaml only.
- **Prod unaffected:** `deploy-vps.yml` already includes `mira-bot-telegram` in its default targets; prod's image is current (2026-07-08, healthy). This changes **staging deploy config only** — no prod behaviour, no app/runtime code, none of the protected files (`engine.py`/`ask_api`/`drive_pack.py`/`ignition_chat.py`).
- **Ops:** staging already redeployed out-of-band (`gh workflow run deploy-staging.yml --ref main -f services=mira-bot-telegram`); `stg-mira-bot-telegram` rebuilt from `main` and healthy. This PR makes that the default so it can't drift again.

### v3.110.1 (2026-07-08) - chore(staging): add stg-mira-tika so OCR/Tika can be proven in staging before prod
- **Why:** the OCR drain path (#2539/#2548) and its `mira-tika` service exist **only** in `docker-compose.saas.yml` (prod). Staging (`docker-compose.staging-vps.yml`) had no Tika and no crawler, so Tika activation could not be proven before prod. This adds a staging mirror so the dev→staging→prod promotion discipline applies to Tika too.
- **What:** new `mira-tika` service (container `stg-mira-tika`) using the **same pinned image** as prod (`apache/tika:3.1.0.0-full`), on `staging-net`. Staging **shares the prod host**, and prod's `mira-tika` already owns host `9998`, so this publishes on **`127.0.0.1:9999:9998`** (loopback-only; container port unchanged). `restart: unless-stopped`, `mem_limit: 1g`, healthcheck on `:9998/tika`.
- **Activation (host-safe staging value):** `TIKA_URL=http://localhost:9999` in Doppler `factorylm/stg` (distinct from prod's `http://localhost:9998`) — set only after `curl http://localhost:9999/tika` returns success. Brought up by the existing `deploy-staging.yml` (`up -d` full stack).
- **Scope/safety:** additive staging-only service; stock image, no build; loopback-bound; prod compose untouched; no drive-pack promotion. Honest caveat: staging still has no crawler, so this proves the **image/service runs and answers** — not end-to-end OCR ingest (that requires the crawler + a real scanned PDF).

### v3.110.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(telegram): nameplate-photo → Drive Commander service-pack answer
- **Gap closed:** a technician on Telegram had no bound asset, so a drive question could only be answered by typing the drive name (`/drive gs10 what is CE10`, #2525/#2526). The reliable context Telegram *does* have is a **nameplate photo**. A nameplate photo **with a question caption** (e.g. a GS10 nameplate + "what does CE10 mean?") now resolves the correct **approved** service pack and returns a cited pack answer — read-only, no LLM fallback, no guessing.
- **New surface-agnostic contract — `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/resolver.py`:** `resolve_service_pack(*, question, drive_name, asset_make_model, nameplate, explicit_pack_id, allow_candidates)` → `PackResolution(pack_id, confidence["high"|"medium"|"none"], source, evidence, reason, ambiguous)`. Pure — no I/O, no DB, no LLM; never raises; **never returns a non-live pack id**. Resolution order `explicit_pack_id → drive_name → question → asset_make_model → nameplate`; the first signal with **exactly one** live-pack match wins, a 0-match signal falls through, and an **ambiguous** signal (>1 live pack named) refuses immediately without trying a weaker signal. Approval is structural: only packs under `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/` (`durapulse_gs10`, `powerflex_525`) are loadable; an explicit candidate id (`powerflex_40`) is refused.
- **Telegram fast path — `mira-bots/telegram/bot.py`:** factored `_format_drive_pack_reply` (now shared with `/drive`); added `_try_nameplate_drive_pack_reply`, hooked at the top of `_dispatch_single_photo`. It reuses the Supervisor's own `NameplateWorker` to **extract** fields only, resolves them via `resolve_service_pack`, and answers via `answer_question`. It only claims the turn on a confident LIVE-pack resolution (or a recognized-manufacturer refusal); every other photo falls through **unchanged** to the existing engine-dispatched flow. Never touches `engine.process`/the FSM.
- **Why no engine-level UNS backstop (carried from #2551):** `uns_context` clobbers `model` with the fault code (GS10→CE10), `product_family` is unset, and `manufacturer` alone is ambiguous — inference from weak UNS state would misroute. The connected-asset fallback stays only where a reliable make/model signal exists (Hub asset-chat, Ignition). Telegram's reliable signal is the nameplate, not inference.
- **Deferred (documented, not a gap):** the two-turn "scan nameplate then ask later" flow — the only per-chat state is the engine's private `conversation_state` (`_load_state`/`_save_state`), so stashing a `pack_id` there would need a forbidden `engine.py` change. The shipped single-message (caption-on-photo) slice is complete; a future multi-turn design must use a dedicated non-engine per-chat KV, not the FSM. Runbook: `docs/drive-commander/telegram-manual-intelligence.md`.
- **Tests:** `tests/test_service_pack_resolver.py` (+11: pack_id, candidate-reject, question, fault-code-doesn't-derail, manufacturer-only-refuse, real ambiguity, nameplate, no-signal, never-raises) and `tests/test_telegram_nameplate_ask.py` (+6: nameplate+caption cited answer, unmatched→won't-guess, manufacturer-only→ask-for-model; `NameplateWorker.extract` mocked, no vision/network). Full drive-pack regression set green (88 passed); ruff clean.
- **Scope/safety:** additive; read-only; no drive writes; no LLM fallback; tenant behavior unchanged. `engine.py`, `ask_api/drive_pack.py`, `ignition_chat.py` untouched (#2526/#2536/#2551 tests stay green).

### v3.109.1 (2026-07-07) - chore(cron): schedule the drive-pack build drain + OCR drain safety-net
- **Wiring, not features.** The two Drive Commander drains shipped in v3.109.0 (#2548/#2549) were both **opt-in workers with no scheduler** — so accepted candidate-builds and quarantined `needs_ocr` PDFs never actually drained on prod. This adds both to `scripts/install_crons.sh`, the source-of-truth crontab installer ("never edit crontab directly — add agents here"), so `bash scripts/install_crons.sh` on the VPS registers them.
- **Drive-pack build drain — `*/15 * * * *`:** `doppler run -- python3 tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/drain_build_requests.py`. Drains the Hub candidate-accept `build_requested` markers → trust-preserving extractor+grader into staged `candidates/` (guarded by `assert_not_live_packs`; **never promotes** to a served pack — human-gated per ADR-0025). No-op when the queue is empty. Run as a script path (the worker does a sibling `import update_candidate`). Issue #2544 / PR #2549.
- **OCR drain safety-net — `30 3 * * *`:** `doppler run -- python3 mira-crawler/cron/kb_growth_cron.py --drain-needs-ocr`. Re-OCRs (via Tika) any `needs_ocr` PDFs that accumulated while Tika was unreachable at ingest time; new scanned PDFs are OCR'd inline by the hourly KB Growth run (#2548), so this only sweeps residue. **INERT until `TIKA_URL=http://localhost:9998` is set in Doppler `factorylm/stg`+`prd`** — the host cron cannot reach the container-DNS default `mira-tika:9998`. Issue #2539 / PR #2548.
- **Activation (operator, human-run):** (1) `doppler secrets set TIKA_URL=http://localhost:9998` in `stg`+`prd`; (2) one-time backlog clear `ssh factorylm-prod "cd /opt/mira && doppler run -- python3 mira-crawler/cron/kb_growth_cron.py --drain-needs-ocr"`; (3) `ssh factorylm-prod "cd /opt/mira && bash scripts/install_crons.sh"` after this deploys. Both entries run under `doppler run --`, so Doppler injects `NEON_DATABASE_URL` / `TIKA_URL`.
- **Scope/safety:** additive crontab entries only; no code path changed; both drains read-only w.r.t. served packs and idempotent.

### v3.109.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(hub): honest KB-gap admission on evidence-less asset-chat (H4 parity, #2542)
- **Gap closed:** `mira-hub/src/app/api/assets/[id]/chat/route.ts` streamed a confident LLM answer even when it had **no** grounding evidence (`manualSources.length === 0` and no fresh live signals) — the trace was merely labeled `kb_gap` while the technician still saw an ungrounded answer. The Python surfaces (Telegram/Slack/Ignition/pipeline) already run the H4 enforcer `enforce_citation_or_gap_admission` (`mira-bots/shared/engine.py` + `citation_compliance.py`) so an uncited reply carries an explicit "I don't have documentation…" admission. This brings the customer-facing Hub surface to parity.
- **Soft, not a hard 412 (product-owner decision):** an evidence-less asset can **still chat** — it just gets an honest KB-gap admission. The existing hard 412 gate stays **opt-in** behind `MIRA_ENFORCE_APPROVED_ASK` / `MIRA_ENFORCE_APPROVED_RETRIEVAL` (default unchanged).
- **Two-layer defense (mirrors quickstart's cite-or-refuse):** new `mira-hub/src/lib/kb-gap.ts` exports (1) `KB_GAP_SYSTEM_INSTRUCTION`, appended to the system prompt when there's no evidence so the model admits the gap up front, and (2) a server-side safety net — after the stream assembles, if the reply has no `[Source:]` citation and no gap phrase, `KB_GAP_ADMISSION` is appended before `[DONE]` so a model that ignores the instruction still can't ship a confident ungrounded answer. Phrasing mirrors the Python `_H4_STOCK_ADMISSION` ("specific documentation indexed", "consult the asset nameplate or vendor manual", "knowledge base").
- **Mechanics:** `streamFromProvider` no longer emits the terminal `[DONE]`; the route now emits a single `[DONE]` after the safety net so the admission always lands inside the rendered response. Retrieval/tenant-scoping (`#2178` hybrid `is_private` filter) untouched; the beta-gate path (a stranger's uploaded manual → cited answer) is unaffected because that path HAS sources (`hasGroundingEvidence === true` → no admission). The **drive-pack pre-check (#2527)** returns before the cascade, so a matched pack answer is never gap-admitted.
- **Tests:** `…/chat/__tests__/route.test.ts` (+5): evidence-less confident answer gets the admission (before `[DONE]`), a model that already admits the gap is not double-admitted, a manual-sourced answer is unchanged, the opt-in 412 gate still refuses when enforcement is on with no context, and the admission phrasing check. Existing chat tests kept green.
- **Scope/safety:** additive to the default path; no branch reordered; read-only; no new hard refusal.

### v3.108.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(hub): candidate accept enqueues pack build+grade (no auto-promote) (#2544)
- **Gap closed:** accepting a `drive_pack_update` `ai_suggestions` row (mig 062) via `/api/suggestions/[id]/decide` → `mira-hub/src/lib/suggestion-accept.ts` was **status-only** — it flipped the row to `accepted` but never ran the extractor+grader. The real work is the Python CLI `tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/update_candidate.py` (classify → family generator → grading harness → staged candidate + report).
- **Shape (enqueue + drain, no synchronous shell-out):** the Hub must not shell out to Python inside an HTTP request, so the work is split. **Enqueue (`suggestion-accept.ts`):** on accept of a `drive_pack_update` suggestion, `markDrivePackBuildRequested()` writes a durable marker onto the row's own `extracted_data` (`build_requested=true`, `build_status='requested'`) — the row IS the queue, no new table/migration. A data annotation, not a status transition (so it does not route through the ADR-0017 helper). Reject enqueues nothing. **Drain (`tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/drain_build_requests.py`):** a standalone worker reads `status='accepted' AND build_requested AND build_status='requested'` rows and invokes `update_candidate.py` (`--manual <local_pdf_path> --id <registry_manual_id>`), then flips `build_status` off `requested` so a marker is drained at most once. DB I/O is injected (`drain(load_requests, save_result, runner=…)`) so the policy core is unit-tested offline; `main()` wires psycopg2 to `NEON_DATABASE_URL`/`DATABASE_URL`.
- **Trust gate preserved:** `update_candidate.py` writes only into the staged `candidates/<family>/` tree, guarded by `assert_not_live_packs()`; the drain passes no `--out` override, so it can NEVER write into the live served `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/` tree. **Auto-promotion candidate→live is forbidden** (ADR-0025, `.claude/rules/train-before-deploy.md`); promotion stays a separate human-gated step (the `candidate_report.md` reviewer checklist + recorded sign-off).
- **Tests:** Python `tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/tests/test_drain_build_requests.py` (7: runner invoked with manual+id and **no** `--out` → never targets `packs/`, rc→built/failed mapping incl. rejected-trust-status review case, missing provenance fails without running, runner-exception caught, `drain` writes a result back for every request + flips off `requested`). Hub `mira-hub/src/lib/__tests__/suggestion-accept.test.ts` (+2: accept writes the durable build-requested marker with no entity; reject enqueues nothing). All 19 registry pytest + 24 Hub vitest green. Design note: `docs/drive-commander/drive-pack-build-enqueue-and-drain.md`.
- **Scope/safety:** additive; the existing kg_entity/tag_mapping accept branches are untouched; read-only, no drive writes, no LLM. The drain is an ops/cron entry, not wired into any customer-facing request path.

### v3.106.0 (2026-07-07) - fix(telegram): route file intake through citable /api/uploads/folder (#2540)
- **Gap closed:** Telegram-uploaded PDFs/photos went to `POST /api/contextualization/import` — a verified dead-end: the route auths with `sessionOr401()` (a Bearer token 401s), its multipart branch expects a `.zip` bundle (a raw PDF/JPEG 400s), and `HUB_IMPORT_URL`/`HUB_IMPORT_TOKEN` are unset in prod so it was dark. Nothing a technician texted the bot ever became citable.
- **Fix:** `contextualization_intake.py` gains `submit_file_to_hub_folder()` (+ `hub_folder_upload_configured()`), which POSTs the raw file to the **working citable door** `POST /api/uploads/folder` with `Bearer HUB_INGEST_TOKEN` + `X-Mira-Tenant-Id` — the same golden path MiraDrop uses (`mira-hub/src/lib/local-upload.ts` → v2 Inbox → `knowledge_entries`, per-tenant `is_private=true`, citable). `mira-bots/telegram/bot.py` photo + document intake now call it; the §2 zip/envelope path is dropped for Telegram. Env-var names match `tools/mira-drop-watcher` (`HUB_URL`/`HUB_BASE_PATH`/`HUB_INGEST_TOKEN`); `HUB_IMPORT_URL` kept only as a back-compat base. Preserves the PDF-only + 20 MB limit and the "Hub intake not configured" graceful skip when env is unset. `docker-compose.saas.yml` wires the new env onto `mira-bot-telegram` (token unset → skip).
- Tests: `mira-bots/tests/test_telegram_hub_intake.py` + `test_telegram_photo_hub_wiring.py` rewritten to assert the `/api/uploads/folder` endpoint, Bearer auth, `X-Mira-Tenant-Id` header, raw-file-not-zip body, per-uploader tenant resolution, and graceful skip when unconfigured (httpx mocked).

### v3.105.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(crawler): OCR-drain needs_ocr PDFs via Tika before quarantine (#2539)
- **Gap closed:** `mira-crawler/cron/kb_growth_cron.py` detected scanned/image-only PDFs (0-char local extraction) and terminally quarantined them `status="needs_ocr"` (#2532) — but **nothing ever drained** `needs_ocr`, so scanned drive manuals could never become a pack (Drive Commander 2/8, audit §6 gap #1). The OCR-capable extractor (`mira-crawler/ingest/converter.py::extract_from_tika`, Apache Tika + Tesseract) existed but was unwired.
- **Fix (fresh 0-char):** before quarantining, the cron re-runs the ingest pipeline with a new `--ocr` flag. `full_ingest_pipeline.step_extract(..., ocr=True)` falls back to `extract_from_tika` when local pdfplumber/pypdf yields no text layer; on success the OCR text continues the **normal** ingest (chunk/embed/KG) via the single pipeline and the entry becomes `done` (+ a drive-pack candidate). Only when OCR is unavailable/empty does it land `needs_ocr`.
- **Fail-safe (safe to merge before `mira-tika` is deployed):** `converter.extract_from_tika` already swallows every error (Tika unreachable/timeout) and returns `[]`; `_attempt_ocr` additionally wraps the subprocess in try/except. An unreachable Tika falls back to the **current** behavior (quarantine `needs_ocr`) — the cron never crashes, never fails loud.
- **Drain (opt-in):** `python3 kb_growth_cron.py --drain-needs-ocr` gives each existing `needs_ocr` entry a one-time OCR retry (→ `done` on success, stays `needs_ocr` with `last_ocr_attempt_at` on failure). A normal hourly cron run is unchanged — it never touches `needs_ocr` entries.
- **No new service:** `mira-tika` already exists in `docker-compose.saas.yml` (on `mira-net`, published `127.0.0.1:9998`). **Deploy step:** set `TIKA_URL=http://localhost:9998` in Doppler `factorylm/stg` + `factorylm/prd` so the host-run cron's pipeline OCR points at the published port (the container-DNS default `http://mira-tika:9998` is only reachable in-network).
- **Tenancy unchanged:** OCR'd manuals follow the same `knowledge_entries` ingest/tenancy as text-layer manuals (`is_private` semantics untouched).
- **Tests:** `mira-crawler/tests/test_kb_growth_ocr_drain.py` (0-char+Tika-success → ingests, not quarantined; 0-char+Tika-empty → `needs_ocr`; 0-char+Tika-unreachable → `needs_ocr` fail-safe; normal + transient-download-failure unchanged; `--drain-needs-ocr` success/still-empty/unreachable/no-op) and `mira-crawler/tests/test_full_ingest_ocr_fallback.py` (pipeline `step_extract` OCR wiring). Existing `test_kb_growth_zero_char_quarantine.py` updated for the new `run_pipeline(entry, ocr=...)` signature. 76 tests pass; ruff clean.

### v3.104.0 (2026-07-07) - fix(slack): route PDF intake through citable /api/uploads/folder (#2543)
- **Gap closed:** `mira-bots/slack/pdf_handler.py::ingest_pdf` wrote Slack uploads **directly** into an Open WebUI knowledge collection (`POST /api/v1/files/` → `/api/v1/knowledge/{id}/file/add`), routed by a filename regex. Per `.claude/rules/knowledge-entries-tenant-scoping.md` the Open-WebUI-KB door is **not** citable on the Hub RAG/NodeChat path — it was a second, divergent ingestion system competing with the system-of-record, so a technician's Slack-uploaded manual never became a citable source.
- **Fix:** `ingest_pdf` now POSTs the raw file to mira-hub's **citable** `/api/uploads/folder` door (Bearer `HUB_INGEST_TOKEN` + header `X-Mira-Tenant-Id`, multipart `file`), matching MiraDrop's request shape (`tools/mira-drop-watcher/main.py`). Uploads land in per-tenant `knowledge_entries` (`is_private=true`) and are citable on the Hub NodeChat path. No new ingestion system — it reuses the existing folder door.
- **Env (consistent with the repo):** `HUB_URL` / `HUB_BASE_PATH` (default `/hub`) / `HUB_INGEST_TOKEN` / `MIRA_TENANT_ID`. The Open-WebUI collection-routing helpers (`_route_collection`, `_get_or_create_collection`) are removed.
- **Preserved:** PDF/image MIME allowlist + a 20 MB size cap (`security-boundaries.md`). When the Hub env is unset the handler logs and returns a graceful "intake isn't configured" message instead of crashing the Slack handler. `bot.py`'s call site is unchanged.
- **Tests:** new `tests/integration/test_slack_pdf_intake.py` (none existed) mocks httpx and asserts the POST hits `/api/uploads/folder` with the Bearer + tenant header and the PDF MIME part, that it gracefully skips with no HTTP call when the env is unset, and that an unsupported MIME is rejected before any call.### v3.103.0 (2026-07-07) - feat: answer the drive pack for the CONNECTED asset without naming the drive (#2527 follow-up)
- **Goal:** a surface bound to a known drive (Hub asset-chat open on a GS10, an Ignition "Ask MIRA" panel bound to a GS10) should answer "what does CE10 mean?" WITHOUT the technician typing "gs10". Two surfaces wired; the third (engine backstop) was investigated and dropped as ineffective (below).
- **Hub asset-chat** (`mira-hub/.../assets/[id]/chat/route.ts` + `mira-bots/ask_api/drive_pack.py`): the drive-pack pre-check now passes the OPEN asset's `manufacturer + model_number` as a `drive` fallback, and the `/drive-pack/ask` endpoint resolves **question-first, drive-fallback** (a drive named in the question still wins; otherwise the bound asset's drive resolves the pack). Folded into the message, not the retrieval query, so it never pollutes RAG recall. +8 tests.

The two surface-level bindings above cover the real deployment paths; no `engine.py` change ships here.

- **Gap closed:** `mira-hub/src/app/api/assets/[id]/chat/route.ts` runs its **own** Groq→Cerebras→Gemini cascade and had zero reference to the drive packs — so a GS10 CE10/P09.03 question in Hub asset-chat got a generic RAG/LLM answer, inconsistent with every **engine** surface (Telegram/Slack/Ignition/pipeline/kiosk, #2526). It resolves the pack (`pack_id` → `drive` → question text via `resolve_pack`) and returns `answer_question(...).to_dict()`. The Hub route calls it as a **pre-check before its LLM cascade** (`route.ts`, immediately after the safety gate): on `matched && answer_source=="drive_pack"` it streams the pack answer + `[Source: … p.X]` citations as SSE and short-circuits; on any miss/timeout/error it falls straight through to the existing cascade unchanged (best-effort, 4 s timeout, `AbortSignal.timeout`).

- **Wiring:** `docker-compose.saas.yml` gives `mira-hub` `MIRA_ASK_URL` (default `http://mira-ask:8011`) + `ASK_API_KEY` (both services already share `mira-net`).

Existing chat tests kept green (fetch mock updated to distinguish the two calls the cascade path now makes).

### v3.100.0 (2026-07-07) - fix(test): un-jam the deploy pipeline — E2E signup-flow strict-locator flake
- **Impact:** the VPS deploy gate had been jammed since v3.92.0 (#2528). `deploy-vps.yml` only runs when Smoke Test concludes `success`, but the `Smoke Test` E2E job failed on **every** commit after #2528 (v3.93.0→v3.99.0), so nothing shipped — including the merged, locally-verified drive-pack `/drive` work. The failure was **unrelated** to any of those commits (0 of them touch `mira-hub`).
- **Root cause:** `mira-hub/tests/e2e/signup-flow.spec.ts` "valid email submits and shows success (or rate-limited on repeat runs)" hits the **live** factorylm.com magic-link form. On repeat CI runs the live site returns 429, and the page renders a **hidden** `#fl-form-success` in the DOM *alongside* the visible `#fl-form-error` ("You requested a link recently. Check your inbox…"). The assertion `expect(success.or(rateLimited)).toBeVisible()` then matched **two** elements → Playwright strict-mode violation → red smoke → gate closed for everyone.
- **Fix:** the two acceptable outcomes are mutually exclusive in *visibility*, so narrow the union with `.filter({ visible: true })` (Playwright 1.59) — exactly one element matches regardless of the 200/429 outcome. Test-only change; no product code touched.
- **Note:** shipped alongside a `skip_staging_gate=true` hotfix dispatch of `mira-bot-telegram`+`mira-pipeline` (drive-pack `/drive` was stuck behind this same jam); this PR restores the normal gated deploy path so the queued crawler fixes (v3.97.0/v3.98.0) and future merges deploy without a bypass.

### v3.99.0 (2026-07-07) - chore(ops): fail2ban SSH-hardening setup script (operator-run, not auto-applied)
- **VPS fail2ban installation script** (`scripts/vps_fail2ban_setup.sh`): idempotent bash script for SSH brute-force protection on Ubuntu/Debian VPS.
- **Configuration:** [sshd] jail with maxretry=5, findtime=10m, bantime=1h; backend=systemd on supported systems.
- **Operator-run only** — does NOT execute automatically. Must be run manually as root on the VPS: `sudo bash scripts/vps_fail2ban_setup.sh`.
- **Critical:** Operator MUST edit ignoreip to include their admin IP + Tailscale subnet before running to avoid self-lockout.
- **Purpose:** respond to 126 MB of failed-login records (btmp) indicating SSH brute-force traffic on production VPS.
- Syntax validated; ready for manual deployment.

### v3.98.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(crawler): quarantine 0-char (scanned) PDFs as needs_ocr instead of retrying
- **Problem:** ingest now extracts PDF text in-process (`mira-crawler/ingest/pdf_extract.py`, pdfplumber→pypdf). For scanned/image-only manuals with no text layer, extraction returns 0 chars with no OCR available — the entry then either retried forever (`failed_retryable`) or eventually burned all `MAX_ATTEMPTS` into a hard `failed`, wasting a cron cycle every hour for a PDF that will never yield text.
- **Fix:** `mira-crawler/cron/kb_growth_cron.py::_process_entry` now detects the exact "produced 0 chars" marker `full_ingest_pipeline.step_extract` appends to `PipelineReport.errors` (rendered in the subprocess's report tail) via a new `_is_zero_char_extraction()` helper, and routes that case straight to a new terminal status `needs_ocr` on the FIRST occurrence — no retry scheduled, no attempt burned. Genuine download/network/transient failures are unaffected (they don't carry the marker) and keep going through `_classify_error()`'s existing retryable/hard path. Text-layer PDFs (chars > 0) are unaffected.
- **Observability:** `_queue_stats()` now reports a `needs_ocr` count; quarantined entries do not count toward `remaining`.
- **Tests:** `mira-crawler/tests/test_kb_growth_zero_char_quarantine.py` (marker detection, quarantine-not-retry, quarantined entries never re-selected, queue-stats count, and regressions proving normal/transient/hard cases are unaffected). Wired into the CI `drive-pack-extract-tests` job's pytest line alongside the existing crawler tests.

### v3.97.0 (2026-07-07) - fix(crawler): stop deploy from clobbering runtime ingest-queue state
- **Bug:** `mira-crawler/cron/kb_growth_cron.py` reads/writes `mira-crawler/cron/manual_queue.json` — the live ingest queue tracking which manuals are pending/done/failed. That file was **tracked in git**, and `deploy-vps.yml` runs `git checkout --force <tag>` on `/opt/mira` on every deploy — silently resetting the live queue's `status`/`attempts`/`done_at` progress back to whatever was last committed, every time.
- **Fix:** stopped tracking `mira-crawler/cron/manual_queue.json` (`git rm --cached`, file stays on disk) and added it to `.gitignore` with a comment explaining why. Runtime queue progress on the VPS now survives deploys.
- **Missing-file safety:** verified `load_queue()` would previously raise `FileNotFoundError` on a missing queue file, and both `run_batch()` and `--status` explicitly `sys.exit(1)`'d in that case — a real risk now that the file isn't guaranteed to exist (fresh box, or right after this change lands). `load_queue()` now returns `[]` when the file is absent so the cron and `--status` self-heal to an empty/sane queue instead of crashing; the redundant exists-checks in `run_batch()`/`--status` were removed since `load_queue()` now owns that case. +3 tests (missing-file `load_queue`, `run_batch`, `--status`); 46 tests green in the cron suite, ruff clean.
- **Scope:** the committed `manual_queue.json` was runtime state (34/35 entries `pending`, one-time initial backlog with mutable `status`/`done_at`/`attempts` fields) — not a curated seed a fresh box needs to hydrate from. No seed-file/hydration mechanism was added; the existing `--hydrate-from-cache` (pulls from NeonDB `manual_cache`) remains the way to (re)populate a queue.

### v3.96.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(engine): deterministic drive-pack fast-path (natural-language GS10 answers across all engine surfaces)
- **Natural conversation, no `/drive` prefix.** A text question that names a drive MIRA has a pack for (e.g. "what does CE10 mean on my gs10") is now answered deterministically from the pack via `shared.drive_packs.answer_question` BEFORE generic router/RAG — reaching **every engine surface at once** (Telegram free-text, Slack, Ignition, the VPS pipeline, the kiosk `/ask`). Builds on `answer_question` (#2523); complements the explicit Telegram `/drive` command (#2525).
- **Trigger is conservative + safe by construction:** fires only when `resolve_pack(message)` matches a drive AND `answer_question(...).matched` is True; otherwise falls through to the existing pipeline completely unchanged (a false-positive `resolve_pack` match is harmless — `matched=False` → fall through).
- **Three verified guardrails** (`mira-bots/shared/engine.py`):
  1. **Placement AFTER the safety short-circuit** — a drive-naming safety utterance ("the gs10 is arc flashing") still returns the safety STOP, never a pack answer.
  2. **Inline `[Source: doc p.X]` citations + `dispatch_kind="drive_pack"`** added to `_TRUSTED_DISPATCH_KINDS` — so the H4 citation/KB-gap enforcer doesn't bolt on a false "not enough information" line and the quality gate doesn't flag the templated text as repetitive.
  3. **Static-vs-live label** — when the turn also carries a live-tag preamble (the kiosk `[LIVE CONVEYOR STATUS]` block OR the Ignition `[LIVE TAGS …]` preamble), the reply is prefixed "Static pack reference — not from live telemetry" so a static pack answer is never conflated with a live read.
- **Tests:** +6 (`mira-bots/tests/test_engine_drive_pack_fastpath.py`), all driving the OUTER `Supervisor.process()`: CE10 cited + no false gap-admission, dispatch_kind, static-label on `[LIVE TAGS]`, safety-wins, non-drive falls through, unmatched falls through. Full engine + `bot_regression` + golden suites: 0 new failures.
- **Scope/safety:** additive fast-path; no existing branch changed; read-only, no drive writes; `answer_question` never calls an LLM. **Follow-up (out of scope):** derive the pack from `state["uns_context"]`/direct-connection asset when the text doesn't name the drive; wire the Hub asset-chat TS cascade.
