### v3.93.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(drive-commander): chapter-section-aware citation verification (unblocks GS10-style page labels)
- **What:** closes the documented cite-integrity gap that kept the GS10 pack's citation category stuck N/A. Some OEM manuals (AutomationDirect DURApulse GS10/GS20) label pages by **chapter-section** ("4-188", "3-6") instead of a running integer page. The int-page `cite_integrity.verify_excerpt_on_page` couldn't parse those, so every such citation was unverifiable.
- **How:** `cite_integrity.is_chapter_section_label()` detects the label form, and `cite_integrity.verify_excerpt_in_document()` verifies the excerpt **whole-document** (it must appear on some page). `cite_check` now dispatches: an integer page is verified page-pinned (strong); a chapter-section label is verified whole-document (weaker but honest — still catches fabrication, tallied separately as `verified_by_label_count`). A fabricated excerpt on a chapter-section page is still unverifiable, and a dropped diagnostic-critical citation still hard-fails.
- **Effect:** a GS10-style pack graded **with a single manual PDF** now scores citation fidelity instead of N/A. (Residual: the GS10 manual ships as separate chapter PDFs, so a merged/single PDF is needed for a full GS10 re-grade; until then GS10 is still graded without a manual and stays INCOMPLETE.)
- **Perf (found + fixed in a pre-close review):** `cite_check` now reads the manual **once** — only the distinct integer pages a pack cites (a pack citing ~6 of a 156-page manual reads 6 pages), or the whole document only when a chapter-section-label citation is present. Previously every citation reopened the 34MB PDF (O(citations × pages)); the new whole-document verify was ~90 s per call. Measured: PF525 cite **~90 s → 1.6 s**, PF40 **52 s → 1.7 s** (`cite_integrity.load_normalized_pages(pdf, pages=…)`).
- **UX (found + fixed in the same review):** `grade_scientific.py` **auto-discovers** `gold/<pack_id>/gold.json` when `--gold` is omitted, so a reviewer can't accidentally grade a pack that HAS a gold set on gold-independent categories only and get a misleadingly low "no gold" / INCOMPLETE verdict (e.g. GS10 read C/75 instead of A/95.2 without `--gold`). `--gold` still overrides; a pack with no gold file is still graded gold-independent.
- **Tests:** +9 (label detection; whole-document verify real vs fabricated; cite_check dispatch verifies a `4-188` citation and still catches fabrication + dropped-critical; `load_normalized_pages` page-scoping; gold auto-discovery). 107 tests green, ruff clean. Docs updated: `GRADING_SPEC.md` §B, GS10 gold `page_numbering`, CI-gate design §2, discovery record.
- **Scope:** grading tool + gold-note + docs only. No runtime change; live packs untouched, no pack promoted, no OEM manual committed.

### v3.92.0 (2026-07-07) - chore(ops): VPS reliability hardening — stale healer entry, flaky stop-gate, ingest overlap guard, weekly docker GC
- **Self-healer stale entry (fix):** removed `mira-docling-saas` from `heartbeat_monitor.CRITICAL_CONTAINERS`. Docling was decommissioned 2026-06-06 (OOM) and is no longer in `docker-compose.saas.yml`, so the self-healer was trying to recreate a non-existent container every 15 min. Ingest now extracts in-process (`mira-crawler/ingest/pdf_extract.py`).
- **Flaky stop-gate (fix):** `tools/hooks/stop-gate.sh` Gate 3 (mira-hub build) now serializes with `flock` (where available) and treats Next's `"Another next build process is already running"` as a **benign race, not a failure** — two overlapping Stop-hook invocations were both running `next build` and racing on the Next build lock, producing spurious "build failed" blocks even though the build compiled cleanly.
- **Ingest overlap guard (automate):** `kb_growth_cron` now wraps its batch in a `singleton_lock` (advisory `fcntl` lock, OS-released on crash so it can't permanently block ingest; a second concurrent run exits cleanly). Prevents an overrunning hourly batch from being double-processed by the next tick. Fail-open if the helper isn't importable.
- **Weekly docker GC (automate):** new `scripts/vps_docker_gc.sh` (build-cache + unused-image prune, before/after log) for a weekly VPS cron — bounds the dangling-image/cache churn that re-accumulates on every deploy.
- **Scope / safety:** ops/reliability only; no product-runtime behavior change. Additive.### v3.91.0 (2026-07-07) - docs(drive-commander): scientific-grading runbook + CI promotion-gate design + discovery record
- **Runbook** (`docs/drive-commander/scientific-grading/runbook.md`): how to run scientific grading locally, read A/B/C/D/F + INCOMPLETE, author a gold set (precision-over-recall, match the pack, don't fake completeness), add a vendor's identifier conventions to the family-aware domain rules, and the five prerequisites before a pack may be promoted (grader measures, humans promote).
- **CI promotion-gate design note** (`ci-promotion-gate-design.md`): the gate blocks a promotion PR (a diff touching `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/*/pack.json`) when a pack is sub-B / INCOMPLETE / hard-gate-fail / critical-failure, scoped to trigger ONLY on promotion paths (not docs/tooling). **Deliberately NOT wired** — documents the two unresolved prerequisites (manuals aren't committed → citation can't run in CI; GS10 chapter-section page labels aren't int-verifiable) with options + a draft workflow, per the mission's "design note, don't force it".
- **Discovery record** (`docs/discovery/2026-07-07-scientific-grading-followups.md`): question, files, commands, results (the P053 float-jitter root cause; GS10 conventions; before/after grades), conclusions, the deterministic workflow, tests/fixtures, and remaining risks.
- **Scope:** docs only. No code, no runtime change, no pack promoted.

### v3.90.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(drive-commander): GS10 scientific gold set + family-aware domain rules (refs #2516)
- **What:** makes the live **durapulse_gs10** pack scientifically gradeable. Two coupled changes close the two blockers the first back-grade exposed. GS10 goes **D/60/INCOMPLETE → A/95.2/INCOMPLETE** — a large, honest improvement, still **not promotable** (citation N/A).
- **GS10 gold set** (`tools/drive-pack-extract/gold/durapulse_gs10/gold.json`): 10 fault codes with GS10 mnemonics (GFF/Lvd/oL/EF/CE1..4/**CE10**), the P09.03 [COM1 Time-out Detection] parameter, and the **CE10 → P09.03** comm-loss link (the AutomationDirect analog of PowerFlex F081→C125 / PF40 F81→A105). Values mirror the manual-cited pack; honestly flags that GS10 is largely `bench_verified` and that its citations use **chapter-section page labels** (`4-188`) the int-page cite-integrity can't verify.
- **Family-aware domain rules** (`grading/domain_rules.py`): ID conventions are now keyed off the pack's declared `family`, NOT a single hardcoded vocabulary. PowerFlex (`A105`/`F081`) and DURApulse (dotted `P09.03`, mnemonic `CE10`) each grade; an **unknown family falls back to the strict PowerFlex pattern** (deliberately NOT a broad relaxation); and the **param-id-leak guard stays absolute** for every family. So a PowerFlex id in a GS10 pack — or a GS10 id in a PowerFlex pack — is still caught as wrong-family contamination. +9 tests proving: PowerFlex still grades, GS10 IDs accepted, all four contamination directions caught, the leak guard holds under GS10 conventions, and unknown families stay strict.
- **GS10 grade (with gold, no manual):** fault + parameter coverage/precision, field accuracy, relationship accuracy, safety all **100**; provenance **50** (truthful — GS10 is mostly bench_verified, so *manual* traceability is genuinely partial); **citation fidelity N/A** (no manual + chapter-section page labels) → **INCOMPLETE, not promotable**. No critical failures. Back-grade report + README updated.
- **Scope:** gold + grading rules + docs only. **No runtime change** — the live `packs/durapulse_gs10/` pack is untouched; no pack promoted. Real OEM manuals never committed. 99 tests green, ruff clean.

### v3.89.0 (2026-07-07) - fix(drive-commander): PowerFlex 525 P053 cross-ref gap (jitter-tolerant detector) + path-free grading reports (refs #2517)
- **Root cause (the real one, not the guessed one):** the scientific back-grade docked PowerFlex 525 to A/98.3 on **fault field accuracy** — only 4 of 6 gold fault→param links resolved. The prior finding blamed "P053 was never extracted"; **that was wrong.** P053 *is* in the pack (page-66 Basic Program grid). The bug was in `extractor._find_cross_refs`: `F100 [Parameter Chksum]` and `F109 [Mismatch C-P]` both say *"Set P053 [Reset To Defaults] to 2/3"* in their action text, but pdfplumber renders the bracket `[Reset` ~0.0003 pt *above* its own id `P053`, so a raw global `(top, x0)` sort placed the bracket *before* the id and the "id immediately followed by `[`" adjacency check silently dropped the reference (`F101` survived only because its tokens tied).
- **Fix:** `_find_cross_refs` now clusters the action band into visual LINES first (the same `_LINE_TOL` tolerance the rest of the extractor already uses) and scans each line in reading order — jitter-tolerant. With the fix `P053.related_faults = [F100, F101, F109]` and all 6 links resolve. Regression test added (`test_find_cross_refs_tolerates_subpixel_top_jitter`, crafted from the real token geometry — the old global-sort returned `[]`). The gold was completed (P053 added as a graded parameter with its fault links). The PF525 F081/F082/F083→C125 and PF40 F81→A105 headline links are unchanged.
- **Proof (grader measures, humans promote — no runtime pack change):** the **live** PF525 pack is UNTOUCHED and still carries the gap — it grades **A/96.9** against the now-complete gold (the gap was slightly undercounted before). The **regenerated staged candidate** (`tools/drive-pack-extract/candidates/powerflex_525/`, trust-status `beta`) grades **A/100**. The live pack reaches 100 only on a separate, human-gated **re-promotion**.
- **Also — path-free grading reports (repeatability):** `grade.py`/`report.py` embedded the manual's ABSOLUTE local path in the committed report (`manual.path` + `extraction_command`) — a machine-specific temp path is noise and a minor local-path leak in a "reproducible" artifact. `report.py` now stores the manual FILENAME only; `grade.py` reduces absolute-path argv tokens to basenames. Both existing committed candidate reports (PF525 new + PF40 regenerated) are now path-free; guard test added.
- **Scope:** grading tool + gold + candidate + docs only. **No runtime change** — the live `packs/powerflex_525/` and `packs/durapulse_gs10/` trees are untouched; no pack promoted. Real OEM manuals never committed. 93 tests green, ruff clean.

### v3.88.0 (2026-07-07) - feat(drive-commander): scientific drive-pack grading rubric (0-100 / A-F) + back-grade of all packs
- **What:** implements `Drive_Pack_Scientific_Grading_Spec` — a deterministic, weighted, numeric (0–100 + A–F) grader that replaces subjective review, on TOP of the existing five-layer harness (which stays the measurement engine). *No drive pack is promoted on subjective review alone. Grade before promote.* **Complements** the existing `beta`/`trusted` trust-status; does not replace it.
- **Rubric (`tools/drive-pack-extract/grading/scientific.py`):** 3 hard gates (schema validity, runtime compatibility — both proven by loading through the real `drive_packs/loader.py` — and provenance presence; any failure → grade **F**, not promotable) + 8 weighted scored categories (provenance 10, fault coverage/precision 20, fault field accuracy 20, param coverage/precision 20, param field accuracy 15, relationship accuracy 10, citation fidelity 15, safety/usability 10). The weights sum to 120, so the overall is a weighted **average** that **renormalizes over gradeable categories** — a pack with no gold set (categories 2–6 N/A) or no manual (citation fidelity N/A) is flagged **INCOMPLETE** and **not promotable** rather than silently scored zero. Grade bands A(92+)/B(82+)/C(70+)/D(50+)/F. Required outputs (spec): overall score+grade, category scores, critical failures, fault/param recall+precision, citation accuracy, missing evidence, promotion recommendation — as machine-readable JSON + human-readable Markdown. Reuses `gold_score`'s `_norm`/`_norm_set` so comparisons match the trust-status path exactly; never re-implements a measurement.
- **CLI (`grade_scientific.py`):** `--gold` is optional (a no-gold pack is graded on gold-independent categories only); exits non-zero when not promotable (a promotion gate). +15 tests (91 in the tool suite, all green; ruff clean) covering band boundaries, weighted-average-over-gradeable, N/A handling, hard gates, critical failures, the relationship-leak floor, and an integration grade of the committed PF40 candidate.
- **Back-grade published (`docs/drive-commander/scientific-grading/`, per the spec's Back-Grading Requirement):** **powerflex_40** (staged candidate) = **A / 100** (full gold + manual 22B-UM001J); **powerflex_525** (live) = **A / 98.3** — the grader precisely caught a real gap (only 4/6 fault→param links present; P053 never extracted); **durapulse_gs10** (live) = **D / 60 / INCOMPLETE, not promotable** — no gold set (coverage/accuracy N/A) AND its non-PowerFlex ID conventions (dotted `P09.03`, `CE10` faults) are flagged by the PowerFlex-oriented domain rules. GS10 not clearing the bar is the intended result: *a pack promoted before this bar existed does not automatically pass it.* Recommendations recorded: author a GS10 gold set + generalize the domain rules for GS10's conventions; extract P053 for PF525.
- **Scope:** grading tool + docs only. No runtime change; the existing `grade.py` trust-status path and all shipped packs are untouched. Real OEM manuals never committed. CI-gate wiring of the scientific grader is a documented follow-up.

- **Scope / safety:** read-only extraction change; no schema/runtime infra change; no OOM risk (in-process pypdf). Deploy re-enables 3 weeks of stalled manual ingest.

### v3.84.0 (2026-07-06) - feat(drive-commander): harden the manual→pack extractor for PowerFlex 40 + staged candidate (beta)
- **What:** the frozen PR-A/B drive-pack extractor was PowerFlex 520/525-specific — run on the real Allen-Bradley **PowerFlex 40** User Manual (22B-UM001J, 156pp) it recovered 46 param IDs but **0 faults + 0 defaults**. Six grounded hardenings (each confirmed against the real PDF) make the same reusable tool parse the PF40 family, proving the manual→pack "compiler" generalizes cross-vendor to a second AB fault-table dialect. Produces a **staged candidate** pack at `tools/drive-pack-extract/candidates/powerflex_40/` — **NOT** the live served `packs/` tree (promotion is a separate, human-gated step per train-before-deploy).
- **Extractor hardenings (`tools/drive-pack-extract/extractor.py`):** (1) **single-digit fault codes** (F2..F8) — the two FAULT-code regexes accept `\d{1,3}`; parameter-id regexes stay `\d{2,3}` (params are never single-digit); (2) **Fault-Type as a position-aware ZapfDingbats circled-digit column** (➀→1 / ➁→2, U+2780/1) rendered ~3pt above its code row, discovered per-page from the glyphs (the "Type" header renders as a garbled reversed ")1(epyT"); (3) **emit untyped faults as "—" instead of dropping** so shared-group continuations (F39/F40) and genuinely untyped faults (F48/F71/F80) still land in the fault map; (4) **label-dialect tolerance** — `(?:Values\s+)?` on both Default and Min/Max ("Values Default: 5.0 Secs" vs "Default:"/"Values Min/Max:"), numeric-only default (worded → honest null), trailing unit captured+normalized; (5) **bold-header gate** — a labeled param header is real only if its pid word is a bold heading font, rejecting a plain-Helvetica graph/curve callout (the PF40 p.71 "A034 [Minimum Freq]" typo that would otherwise pass cite-integrity); generalizes PR-B's hardcoded page-98 skip; (6) **"Options"-prefixed enum** first line + inline unit polish + **wrapped "Related Parameters:" continuation** recovery (kept out of purpose).
- **Also:** a **fault-page-identity gate** (a page is a fault table only if it carries BOTH the Description and Action headers) preserves the "no fabricated faults on a param page" guarantee that emit-not-drop would otherwise break; **span-containment** cross-ref attribution on the dingbat layout so the headline **F81 [Comm Loss] → A105 [Comm Loss Action]** link — the cross-vendor comm-loss proof (analog of GS10 CE10→P09.03 and PF525 F081→C125) — attributes to the right fault (a long numbered action list runs below the code line, where nearest-by-top misattributes it).
- **Real-manual trust doctrine:** the discovered messiness is folded into the synthetic CI fixture (`_make_pf_sample_pdf.py`, two new PF40 pages: dingbat Fault-Type column, single-digit codes, shared/untyped rows, wrapped name, PF40 label dialect, Options-prefix enum, a plain-Helvetica graph callout to reject, a wrapped Related-Parameters list) using an embedded circled-digit glyph subset. The real PF40 PDF is **never committed**. +15 extractor tests (76 total), ruff clean. An **independent** real-manual re-run + JSON inspection (trust-gate step 3) verified all 35 cites verbatim and found/fixed one blemish (the wrapped Related-Parameters continuation).
- **Candidate grade (`grading/grade.py` against the real manual):** schema PASS · cite-integrity **35 verified / 0 unverifiable** · gold overall recall **100%** / precision **100%** · diagnostic-critical recall+precision **100%** · fault recall **100%** · **0 fabrications** · domain rules clean → **TRUST STATUS = `beta`** (the automated ceiling for a manual-cited-only pack; `trusted` needs a recorded human sign-off). Artifacts: `gold/powerflex_40/gold.json`, `generate_pf40_pack.py`, `candidates/powerflex_40/{pack.json,PROVENANCE.md,grading_report.{md,json}}`.
- **Scope:** extractor tool + staged candidate + gold only. Runtime `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/` is untouched; `resolve_pack("PowerFlex 40")` is unchanged in production (no promotion).

### v3.82.0 (2026-07-06) - feat(crawler): default-OFF bridge — successful manual KB ingest → review-only drive-pack update candidate
- **What:** wires the manual-discovery fleet to the trust-graded drive-pack path. When `kb_growth_cron` successfully ingests a manual PDF into the KB, a new **default-off** bridge optionally creates a **review-only drive-pack update candidate** — iff the PDF maps to a known drive family and its hash is new/changed. **Acceptance:** *the bridge turns successful manual KB ingest into a reviewable drive-pack update candidate, but it cannot promote or replace a trusted pack.*
- **Insertion point:** `mira-crawler/cron/kb_growth_cron.py::_process_entry` success branch (only place with mfr/model + the downloaded PDF in scope). The call site is a small `try/except` that **fails open** — a bridge error never fails the already-successful KB ingest.
- **Logic (`mira-crawler/drive_pack_bridge.py`, injectable/testable):** default-OFF behind `MIRA_DRIVE_PACK_BRIDGE=1`; honors `~/.mira/STOP_INGEST`; inherits the cron's batch throttle. Locates the PDF read-only by mirroring the pipeline's cache convention (`MANUALS_ROOT/{mfr}/{model}/{basename}.pdf`); computes the PDF SHA-256; maps `(manufacturer, model)` → a `registry/sources.json` entry (match on model, since discovery says "Allen-Bradley" while the registry says "Rockwell"); classifies via the PR #2507 registry — `unchanged` → no-op, `changed_by_hash`/`needs_initial_candidate` → candidate.
- **Candidate record (review-only):** written to `~/.mira/drive-pack-candidates/<manual_id>/candidate-<sha12>.json` (override `MIRA_DRIVE_PACK_CANDIDATE_DIR`) — NEVER under `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/` or the committed `candidates/` tree. Hard `trust_status:"candidate"`, `promoted:false`, `review_only:true`. Provenance-complete: manufacturer, model, manual_id, vendor, product_family, publication, revision, source_url, pdf_sha256, previously_registered_sha256, ingest_timestamp, local_pdf_path, and the exact `next_step` command to extract+grade. It does NOT run the extractor/grader inline.
- **Trust-preserving:** a changed manual creates a candidate, never replaces a trusted pack; extraction/grading/cite-integrity/domain + human approval remain required before any trusted-pack change; the old pack stays live. No runtime DriveSense behavior change; no KB-ingest dependency on candidate creation.
- **Tests:** 15 offline tests (`mira-crawler/tests/test_drive_pack_bridge.py`) — bridge-disabled-no-op, STOP_INGEST-prevents-work, missing-PDF-fail-open, no-mapping-fail-open-with-report, unchanged-no-candidate, changed→candidate, new-known→candidate, never-targets-trusted-packs, review-only-not-trusted, writes-only-under-candidate-dir, bridge-failure-fails-open, provenance-complete. Wired into the `drive-pack-extract-tests` CI job.
- **Docs:** `docs/runbooks/manual-kb-ingest-to-drive-pack-bridge.md`, `docs/drive-commander/workflow-create-candidate-from-discovered-manual.md`; updated `runbook-do-not-silently-trust-updated-manuals.md` + flipped `bridge-manual-discovery-to-drive-pack-grading.md` from design → implemented.
- **Scope / safety:** no new crawler, no new scheduler, additive, default-off, read-only w.r.t. packs. All 61 drive-pack+crawler offline tests green.

### v3.80.0 (2026-07-06) - feat(drive-commander): manual source registry + trust-preserving update-candidate workflow
- **What:** turns DriveSense manual→pack ingestion from one-off extraction into a **repeatable, trust-preserving update loop** — without building a second ingestion product. Answers the "keep drive manuals/packs current" brief by *reusing* the merged extractor (#2503) + grader (#2505) verbatim and adding only the thin update spine that was missing: a manual **source registry**, a read-only **change-detection** command, and a **candidate** generator. Core rule: *a changed vendor PDF creates a candidate, never an automatic trusted pack* — so an OEM manual revision can't silently rewrite MIRA's diagnostic truth.
- **Discovery first (doctrine):** a repo-wide inventory of every existing ingest/proposal/update path precedes the build — `docs/drive-commander/discovery-manual-ingest-and-update-workflow.md`. Findings: the extractor/grader/trust machinery already exists; the doc-ingest citable path is Hub node-ingest v2 (`knowledge_entries`); the proposal/approval state machine (ADR-0017 `ai_suggestions`) can host a future review item; SHA-256 hash primitives + a scheduled KB cron already exist. The only real gaps were manual-identity, hash-tied-to-pack change detection, and an update-candidate concept — all additive.
- **New (`tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/`):** `sources.json` (human-curated manual registry — vendor/model/publication/revision, approved `pdf_sha256`, generator+gold, trust status, residuals, approval record; **no PDF committed**), `registry.py` (pure load/validate + duplicate-identity detection + `classify()` state machine: `new_manual`/`unchanged`/`changed_by_hash`/`needs_initial_candidate`), `check.py` (read-only, non-gating: hash a local PDF → classify), `update_candidate.py` (reuses the existing generator + `grading/grade.py` as subprocesses → writes `candidate_report.{json,md}` with source identity + Phase-6 grading fields + pack-diff-vs-previous + reviewer checklist).
- **Trust-preserving by construction:** `update_candidate` writes **only** under `candidates/` (`assert_not_live_packs` refuses the live served `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/` tree), hard-codes `promoted: false`, and inherits the grader's automated ceiling of `beta` (`trusted` needs a recorded human sign-off). A `manual-review-only` source (`automatable:false`, e.g. GS10 today) is refused, not half-run.
- **Docs (Phase 7):** `docs/drive-commander/{workflow-register-a-manual-source,workflow-check-for-manual-updates,runbook-drive-manual-update-acceptance,runbook-do-not-silently-trust-updated-manuals,runbook-rss-product-update-adapter}.md` + the discovery record. RSS/OEM-feed automation is explicitly **staged behind the registry**, not built (the bulk crawler was disabled twice for VPS incidents #1318/#1336).
- **Tests (Phase 8, CI-safe):** 27 new offline tests (`registry/tests/`) — registry parse, automatable-requires-generator/gold, duplicate-identity fail-closed, SHA-256 determinism/change, classify state machine, no-auto-promote, no-live-packs guard, report carries provenance+trust, pack-diff. Wired into the `drive-pack-extract-tests` CI job (synthetic only; full-manual runs stay local). "Param-ids never in `related_faults`" / "unverifiable excerpts dropped" remain enforced by the reused grader + its existing tests.
- **Scope / safety:** additive, zero runtime change. Only new files under `tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/`, 5 docs + 1 discovery doc, one CI line, VERSION + CHANGELOG. No edits to the extractor/grader/schema/loader, engine, Hub, DB, or any pack. Read-only, no control writes, no manual committed. All existing 62 drive-pack tests stay green.
### v3.79.3 (2026-07-06) - fix(hooks): exempt rebase --continue/--abort/--skip/--quit from git-state-guard's mid-rebase block
- **Problem:** `tools/hooks/git-state-guard.sh` blocks git mutators while mid-rebase, but its mutator regex matched `git rebase` unconditionally — including the `--continue`/`--abort`/`--skip` invocations that are the ONLY way to resolve the wedge. A single Bash tool call doing `git rebase --continue` while mid-rebase was denied outright. The hook's own documented escape hatch (`MIRA_ALLOW_GIT_WEDGE=1`) doesn't help here either: the hook evaluates the submitted command text before any of it executes, so `export MIRA_ALLOW_GIT_WEDGE=1 && git rebase --continue` in one call is evaluated with the var still unset.
- **Fix:** new `RESOLVER` regex matches `--continue|--abort|--skip|--quit` on `rebase`/`cherry-pick`/`revert`/`am` and allows those through even while mid-rebase — they resolve the wedge, they don't create one. A plain `git commit`/`git rebase <target>` while mid-rebase is still denied as before.
- **Verified manually** (no existing test harness for this hook): built a throwaway repo with a fake `.git/rebase-merge/` marker and confirmed `git rebase --continue`, `--abort`, and `--skip` are now allowed (no deny output) while `git commit -m test` is still denied with the original message.
- **Scope:** one file, `tools/hooks/git-state-guard.sh`. No change to the detached-HEAD branch or the mutator list. shellcheck clean.

### v3.79.2 (2026-07-06) - feat(ci): migration CHECK constraint drift guardrail
- Adds `tools/check_migration_check_drift.py`, a READ-ONLY drift detector that prevents silent CHECK constraint value shrinkage (regression like migration 032's near-loss of 31 enum values → 28). Parses CHECK constraints from new/modified `.sql` migration files and diffs their declared values against the live staging database schema via `information_schema.check_constraints`.
- **Wired into `migration-verify.yml`** as a post-apply, pre-verification gate: fails (returns 1) if any migration declares a SUBSET of live constraint values (specific missing values named in error). Growth (values added) always passes. New constraint (not yet live) passes.
- **Pattern reuse:** extends the drift-check precedent established by `db-inspect.yml`'s 2026-06-24 ingest-schema probe; same READ-ONLY, staging-only architecture.
- **Tests:** 11 unit tests (parse inline/ALTER CHECK, multiline IN clauses, empty/missing, shrink/growth/unchanged detection); parser tests pure-logic (no DB). Parser accepts both inline `CREATE TABLE foo ( col CHECK (col IN ...))` and `ALTER TABLE ADD CONSTRAINT foo_check CHECK (...)` syntax.
- **Scope:** CI enforcement + awareness; does not gate the migration apply (staged after) but blocks the merge if drift is detected. Zero impact to existing migration code or schema design.

### v3.79.0 (2026-07-06) - feat(drive-commander): manual source registry + trust-preserving update-candidate workflow
- **What:** turns DriveSense manual→pack ingestion from one-off extraction into a **repeatable, trust-preserving update loop** — without building a second ingestion product. Answers the "keep drive manuals/packs current" brief by *reusing* the merged extractor (#2503) + grader (#2505) verbatim and adding only the thin update spine that was missing: a manual **source registry**, a read-only **change-detection** command, and a **candidate** generator. Core rule: *a changed vendor PDF creates a candidate, never an automatic trusted pack* — so an OEM manual revision can't silently rewrite MIRA's diagnostic truth.
- **Discovery first (doctrine):** a repo-wide inventory of every existing ingest/proposal/update path precedes the build — `docs/drive-commander/discovery-manual-ingest-and-update-workflow.md`. Findings: the extractor/grader/trust machinery already exists; the doc-ingest citable path is Hub node-ingest v2 (`knowledge_entries`); the proposal/approval state machine (ADR-0017 `ai_suggestions`) can host a future review item; SHA-256 hash primitives + a scheduled KB cron already exist. The only real gaps were manual-identity, hash-tied-to-pack change detection, and an update-candidate concept — all additive.
- **New (`tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/`):** `sources.json` (human-curated manual registry — vendor/model/publication/revision, approved `pdf_sha256`, generator+gold, trust status, residuals, approval record; **no PDF committed**), `registry.py` (pure load/validate + duplicate-identity detection + `classify()` state machine: `new_manual`/`unchanged`/`changed_by_hash`/`needs_initial_candidate`), `check.py` (read-only, non-gating: hash a local PDF → classify), `update_candidate.py` (reuses the existing generator + `grading/grade.py` as subprocesses → writes `candidate_report.{json,md}` with source identity + Phase-6 grading fields + pack-diff-vs-previous + reviewer checklist).
- **Trust-preserving by construction:** `update_candidate` writes **only** under `candidates/` (`assert_not_live_packs` refuses the live served `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/` tree), hard-codes `promoted: false`, and inherits the grader's automated ceiling of `beta` (`trusted` needs a recorded human sign-off). A `manual-review-only` source (`automatable:false`, e.g. GS10 today) is refused, not half-run.
- **Docs (Phase 7):** `docs/drive-commander/{workflow-register-a-manual-source,workflow-check-for-manual-updates,runbook-drive-manual-update-acceptance,runbook-do-not-silently-trust-updated-manuals,runbook-rss-product-update-adapter}.md` + the discovery record. RSS/OEM-feed automation is explicitly **staged behind the registry**, not built (the bulk crawler was disabled twice for VPS incidents #1318/#1336).
- **Tests (Phase 8, CI-safe):** 27 new offline tests (`registry/tests/`) — registry parse, automatable-requires-generator/gold, duplicate-identity fail-closed, SHA-256 determinism/change, classify state machine, no-auto-promote, no-live-packs guard, report carries provenance+trust, pack-diff. Wired into the `drive-pack-extract-tests` CI job (synthetic only; full-manual runs stay local). "Param-ids never in `related_faults`" / "unverifiable excerpts dropped" remain enforced by the reused grader + its existing tests.
- **Scope / safety:** additive, zero runtime change. Only new files under `tools/drive-pack-extract/registry/`, 5 docs + 1 discovery doc, one CI line, VERSION + CHANGELOG. No edits to the extractor/grader/schema/loader, engine, Hub, DB, or any pack. Read-only, no control writes, no manual committed. All existing 59 drive-pack tests stay green.

### v3.79.1 (2026-07-06) - fix(hooks): scope Stop hook to session-touched files + add worktree file-placement guard
- **Problem:** Stop hook blocked on peer-committed files in the shared working tree (diffs against `origin/main...HEAD` in concurrent multi-session checkout; other sessions' commits got lint-gated against this session's Stop hook, blocking completion on pre-existing unrelated errors). Also, sessions/subagents wrote files into the wrong git worktree with no detection.
- **Fix 1 — Stop hook scoping:** PostToolUse Edit|Write hook now logs each file to a per-session touched-files set (`${GITDIR}/claude-sessions/${SESSION_ID}-touched-files`). stop-gate.sh intersects `CHANGED` with this log (if it exists), gating only on files THIS session actually touched, falling back to the old origin/main...HEAD behavior when log absent (backward compat for overnight/headless runs).
- **Fix 2 — worktree guard:** new PreToolUse Write|Edit hook (`tools/hooks/worktree-file-guard.sh`) warns (never blocks) when a Write/Edit targets a file in a different git working tree than the current shell, with clear "current vs. target" messaging. Skips `/tmp`, non-repo targets, and the normal case (same toplevel).
- **Scope / safety:** read-only for Fix 2; Fix 1 is append-only on the touched-files log. No changes to the git dag or commit paths. Backward compatible for sessions without the log (fall back to old behavior). Insights-report friction category 3 ("Environmental Guardrails"), two of three identified issues.

### v3.78.0 (2026-07-06) - feat(drive-commander): PowerFlex 525 pack + reproducible trust/grading workflow (PR-B)
- **What:** PR-B — the cross-vendor proof that the drive-pack loop generalizes to a drive we did NOT seed. Runs the PR-A extractor **offline** on the real PowerFlex 525 manual (`520-UM001O-EN-E`) → a **STAGED CANDIDATE** `tools/drive-pack-extract/candidates/powerflex_525/pack.json` — validated + graded there, but deliberately **NOT** added to the live served `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/` tree, so there is genuinely **no runtime resolver behavior change**: `resolve_pack("PowerFlex 525")` still returns `None` in production. Promotion of a graded candidate into the live tree is a separate, future, human-gated deploy step (`.claude/rules/train-before-deploy.md`; see "Promotion (candidate → live)" in `docs/drive-commander/runbook-pr-b-acceptance.md`). The actual deliverable of this PR is an **open, reproducible grading workflow** that decides whether generated JSON is trustworthy. Doctrine: *"The drive pack is not trusted because the extractor ran; it is trusted only when reproducible checks prove the JSON matches the source PDF within declared limits"* (`docs/drive-commander/drive-pack-trust-doctrine.md`).
- **The pack (`schema_version: 2`, manual-cited-only):** 48 fault codes (F000–F127) + 45 diagnostic parameters, all `manual_cited`. The cross-vendor parallel to GS10 CE10→P09.03 is intact and cited: **F081/F082/F083 "Comm Loss" → C125 [Comm Loss Action]** (page 162/102), with C126 [Comm Loss Time] (default 5.0s, 0.1/60.0). `live_decode.status_bits`/`cmd_word`/`registers` + `envelope` are **empty** — PowerFlex 525 has no bench data, nothing invented. Generated by the new offline `tools/drive-pack-extract/generate_pf525_pack.py` (reproducible; manual gitignored, never committed; sha256 recorded in `PROVENANCE.md`).
- **The grading harness (`tools/drive-pack-extract/grading/`, the real deliverable):** a fail-closed, 5-layer, reproducible workflow — **A** schema (reuses the runtime loader's own `_parse_pack` validation logic, run against the staged candidate directory), **B** cite-integrity (re-reads the PDF, drops unverifiable excerpts), **C** gold-set scoring vs a human-approved `gold/powerflex_525/gold.json` (precision over recall; fabrication = a value contradicting gold or a param-id leaked into `related_faults`), **D** deterministic domain rules (fault-codes-are-fault-codes, no param-id in `related_faults`, no dup ids, uncited-value guard, mandatory `view_only_warning`, provenance vocabulary), **E** a machine- + human-readable report that assigns exactly one trust status: `rejected | internal_only | beta | trusted`. `grade.py` exits non-zero on `rejected`. 25 grading self-tests + 32 extractor tests = **57 offline tests**, now wired into CI (`drive-pack-extract-tests`, synthetic 4KB fixture only — full-manual grading is a documented local command).
- **Verified result — TRUST STATUS: `beta`** (the correct automated ceiling for a manual-cited-only pack; `trusted` requires a recorded human sign-off per `runbook-pr-b-acceptance.md`). Grading report (committed as acceptance evidence next to the pack): schema PASS · cite-integrity **93 verified / 0 unverifiable** · gold-scoring **100% recall + precision, diagnostic-critical 100%, 0 fabrications** · domain PASS · 3 residuals declared honestly.
- **Anti-fabrication in action:** the orchestrator independently re-ran the extractor on the real manual and inspected the JSON (the 10-step gate). Two honest sanitizations were applied at generation (not by weakening a check): 6 cross-row-bleed `default`/`unit` fields (P045/P052/…) nulled to honest "unknown"; and the messy multi-column page-98 analog-output block (which produced a duplicate `t089`) deliberately excluded and declared a residual rather than shipping bleed. A fail-closed uniqueness guard refuses to emit a pack with duplicate parameter-ids.
- **Declared residuals (honest):** F100/F109→P053 fault→param links not recovered by the extractor (non-diagnostic-critical); page-98 analog-output block deferred (extractor-hardening = PR-A scope); `related_parameters` (e.g. C125→P045) not represented — `ParameterCard` has no such field (deferred to a runtime schema PR).
- **Docs/runbooks (required deliverable):** `docs/drive-commander/{drive-pack-trust-doctrine,workflow-generate-drive-pack,workflow-grade-drive-pack,runbook-pr-b-acceptance,runbook-adding-a-drive-family}.md`.
- **Scope / safety:** additive. Only new files under `tools/drive-pack-extract/{generate_pf525_pack.py,grading/,gold/,candidates/,.gitignore}`, the 5 docs, one CI job, VERSION + CHANGELOG. **Nothing lands under `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/packs/`** — the staged candidate is deliberately outside the live served tree, so `resolve_pack()` behavior is unchanged and the existing `test_resolve_pack_returns_none_for_unrelated_drive` test (which asserts `resolve_pack("PowerFlex 525") is None`) stays green as-is. No edits to the extractor, `schema.py`/`loader.py`/`cards.py`, engine, Hub, DB, or any existing pack. All 22 drive-packs runtime tests stay green. Read-only, no control writes, no manual committed. **Stacked on PR-A (#2503); rebase onto main after it merges.**

### v3.77.0 (2026-07-06) - feat(drive-commander): manual→pack extraction tool + cite-integrity framework (PR-A)
- **What:** the reusable **offline** compiler that turns an OEM drive-manual PDF into structured, cited drive-pack data — the tooling that makes new drive families (PowerFlex, Yaskawa, …) cheap. New package `tools/drive-pack-extract/`; does NOT touch the runtime `mira-bots/shared/drive_packs/` package (stays pure + read-only-gated), engine, Hub, DB, or any shipped pack. This is **PR-A ("the parser works")**; the actual PowerFlex service pack is a separate, human-approved PR-B ("the pack is trusted").
- **Position-aware extraction (not `extract_tables()`):** regex-anchored parsers over pdfplumber `extract_words()` x/y coordinates recover columns that `extract_text()`/`extract_tables()` silently drop. Handles the real PowerFlex 520-UM001 messiness: footnote markers glued to fault names, shared-description multi-code fault rows (F038/F039/F040), the `Fault Type (1/2)` column, and two different parameter layouts (grid + labeled-block).
- **The correctness guarantee — `related_faults` holds only FAULT codes.** A fault's "Modify using C125" action populates the parameter's `related_faults` with the FAULT code (C125→[F081,F082,F083]); a parameter's own "Related Parameters:" line is kept separately as `related_parameters` and never conflated. Worded/model-variant ranges are honestly kept `None` rather than fabricated.
- **Cite-integrity (anti-fabrication):** every emitted entry carries a page + verbatim excerpt, and `verify_excerpt_on_page` re-reads that PDF page — the extractor DROPS any entry whose excerpt can't be verified, so a fabricated citation is impossible. Self-test with teeth (a fabricated excerpt is rejected).
- **Page-range scoping + perf:** `extract(pdf, fault_pages=…, param_pages=…)` scopes by page number on the original PDF (preserving per-page geometry, so fault-type recovery survives). Whole-doc scan (>280s timeout) → **~4s scoped**; a second perf layer (cite-integrity reopening the 33 MB PDF per entry) was found + fixed.
- **Acceptance = real-manual trust, not synthetic correctness.** Verified INDEPENDENTLY against the real PowerFlex 520-UM001: 48 faults with clean names + recovered types, 35 params with recovered numeric ranges (worded ones honestly None), `related_faults` = fault codes only across all params, cite-integrity enforced, ~4s. Documented honest residuals (README): P045/P052 conditional-default bleed; minor header-furniture bleed into one `action` field. The real manual is NOT committed; CI runs against a small synthetic fixture that reproduces the discovered messiness. 32 tests, ruff clean.

### v3.73.1 (2026-07-05) - feat(drivesense): schema v2 cards for parameters and keypad navigation
- **What:** DriveSense PR B — **schema/types only**. Adds the type layer for cited configurable-parameter decode and view-only keypad navigation, so a later phase can populate them without touching live diagnosis now.
- **New pack-stored shapes (`drive_packs/schema.py`):** `ParameterCard` (cited view of one configurable parameter — the keypad/manual id like `P09.03`, NOT a Modbus register; carries `value_meanings`/`default`/`range`/`unit`/`related_faults`/citation/provenance), `KeypadNavigationCard` (ordered **view-only** button-press steps; `view_only_warning` is mandatory + non-empty as a safety contract; `keypad_steps` are display strings, never executable), and `ValueMeaning`. `Citation` relocated here (from `cards.py`, re-exported for back-compat) so the pack-stored cards can reference it without a schema→cards import cycle.
- **schema_version 2 (`drive_packs/loader.py`):** the loader now accepts `{1, 2}` (unknown version → hard error, never a silent parse) and parses two OPTIONAL top-level blocks — `parameters` + `keypad_navigation` — into the new cards, injecting `drive_family` from `pack_id`. Enforces the closed provenance vocabulary (`bench_verified`|`manual_cited`, never bare "verified") and the non-empty `view_only_warning`. A pure `_parse_pack(raw, pack_id, path)` seam was split out for dict-level testing. **v1 packs load unchanged** (the real `durapulse_gs10` stays v1; new fields default empty).
- **`DriveDiagnostic` (`live_snapshot.py`):** extended with two additive carry slots — `related_parameters: list[ParameterCard] = []` and `keypad_navigation: KeypadNavigationCard | None = None`. `build_drive_diagnostic` does **not** populate them yet, so the existing assessment + fault-card rendering is **byte-identical** (existing tests green, unchanged).
- **Scope / safety:** pure schema/types — no manual parsing, no runtime keypad guidance, no DB/network/socket, no Hub/Slack/Telegram/Ignition surface change, no runtime dependency on the (open, docs-only) PR #2494. Read-only AST gate stays green. Explicitly deferred (proposal §4/§5, not in this PR): populating the new fields in `build_drive_diagnostic`, the `evidence`/`unknowns`/`safety_warning` response fields, and the extended `Citation` (`section`/`chunk_id`/`tier`).
- **Tests:** `mira-bots/tests/test_drive_packs_schema_v2.py` (13) — v1 still loads (empty blocks), v2 parses from dict + disk, card fields + `drive_family` injection, unsupported-version / empty-warning / missing-`parameter_id` / bad-provenance rejection, `Citation` re-export identity, and `DriveDiagnostic` additive-fields-default-empty + frozen. Full drive-pack + live-snapshot surface **95 green** (incl. readonly gate + byte-identical rendering); ruff clean.

### v3.70.1 (2026-07-05) - docs(skills): add PR/merge-state re-verification doctrine to ship-pr and ship skills
- **What:** the `ship-pr` and `ship` skills now include a **double-read-and-compare pattern** for GitHub API calls when making merge-adjacent decisions. GitHub's API cache lag (up to ~5 seconds on status changes) can cause a single `gh pr checks` or `gh pr view` read to conflict with actual state or prior user reports — particularly when a merge just landed. Both skills now mandate: if a single API read conflicts with expectation or prior information, **always re-fetch after a 2-second delay** and act only when two independent reads agree.
- **Doctrine:** the `ship-pr` skill adds §4b on "API cache lag: the insights-report pattern", citing the 2026-06-08 insights report's concrete example (merge reported ✓ → API shows OPEN → subsequent re-checks confirm the merge). The `ship` skill embeds re-verify guidance into the merge step itself (§4), instructing the operator to check `gh pr view <PR#> --json state,mergeable` before acting if any conflict arises.
- **Why:** this is a response to friction pattern #2 from the 2026-07-05 insights deployment (GitHub cache lag + concurrent-session edits = silent loss of ground truth). No code change; process-only. Allows merges + deploys to be safer under high-latency API reads.

### v3.70.2 (2026-07-05) - fix(ci): guard unguarded pipes in pre-commit hook against SIGPIPE (section 7b)
- **What:** fixes a critical hook failure when the `.git/` working tree contains a large number of untracked files (50k+). The section-7b diagnostic message `printf '%s\n' "$UNTRACKED" | head -5 | sed` would abort with exit 141 (SIGPIPE) when the buffer overflowed before `head -5` closed the read side of the pipe.
- **The fix:** guards all 7 unguarded pipes in the script with `|| true` (lines 94, 104, 105, 132, 236, 255, 266). SIGPIPE is a normal pipe-closure condition — the message is informational and the hook MUST NOT fail on it. `|| true` also guards the `echo | wc -l` on line 105 to be safe.
- **Verification:** pre-commit now exits 0 on the large-untracked scenario; reproduction test confirms exit 141 before, 0 after. All other checks unchanged. ruff clean.

### v3.70.0 (2026-07-05) - feat(drive-commander): Ignition analog assessment via an explicit per-tag scaling contract (follow-up #2)
- **What:** the Ignition direct "Ask MIRA" path can now assess **analog** live values (DC bus / current / frequency) against the GS10 pack envelope — but **only when the tag carries an explicit, verified scaling contract**. Before this, analog values were shown in the preamble but never assessed, because a wire value like `vfd_dc_bus = 3200` is ambiguous (raw register ×0.1 → 320 V, or already 320 V). Envelope assessment already shipped on the *engine* snapshot path (v3.65.0); this closes it on the *Ignition wire* path without reintroducing the ambiguous-scaling risk.
- **The contract (new pure layer `mira-bots/shared/wire_scaling.py`):** `TagScaling{mode, scale, unit, source}` with `mode ∈ {raw_register, engineering_value, unknown}`. `to_engineering()` converts a wire value ONLY when the mode is explicit (a `raw_register` tag with no `scale` inherits the pack's trusted register scaling); `unknown`/missing/un-coercible ⇒ `None` ⇒ the caller stays silent. `from_jsonb()` reads the value from `tag_entities.scaling` (contract shape `{"mode":"raw_register","scale":0.1}`; a `NULL`/mode-less value ⇒ `unknown`, never a guess).
- **Assessment (`live_snapshot.assess_analog_from_paths`):** a **separate, opt-in** function beside `assess_from_paths` — the enum/bool hard boundary is untouched (analog leaves are still NOT in the assessable sets). It reuses the existing pack envelope via a new structured `_analog_band_status` helper (the engine path's `_analog_band_observation` was refactored onto it, behavior-preserving). Renders a **self-explaining card**: `DC bus: 320 V / Source value: 3200 / Scaling: raw register ×0.1 (approved tag mapping) / Normal band: 300–340 V / Assessment: normal`. A tag with an explicit scale but no full pack band (e.g. `current`) stays silent — honest abstention (ADR-0025 §4).
- **Wire seam (`mira-pipeline/ignition_chat.py`):** the existing verified-`tag_entities` enrichment SELECT now also reads `scaling` (a read; no new write path); the endpoint builds `{path → TagScaling}` and appends the analog card(s) after the enum/bool assessment. Best-effort/never-raises; unknown/missing scaling ⇒ no card ⇒ prior display-only behavior.
- **Scope / safety:** read-only/offline (no DB write, no socket, no fieldbus); the read-only shipping gate stays green. Explicitly deferred (documented): populating `tag_entities.scaling`/`expected_envelope` for real tenants, the Hub TS mirror, component-template citation pointers on the card, per-component UNS granularity.
- **Tests:** `mira-bots/tests/test_wire_scaling.py` (12, pure contract) + `test_live_snapshot_analog_paths.py` (11: raw/eng/unknown/missing/out-of-band/pack-fallback/no-band-silent/ambiguous-3200-no-false-undervoltage) + 2 route tests proving the card reaches (and unknown scaling withholds) the Ignition prompt end-to-end. mira-bots 100 green (engine/live-snapshot/drive-pack regression unchanged = byte-identical engine path); mira-pipeline Ignition 14 green. ruff clean.

### v3.64.0 (2026-07-05) - feat(ignition): deterministic live-tag Assessment on the HMI Ask-MIRA surface
- **What:** brings the deterministic **Assessment** (from #2476 Hub / #2478 engine) to the **Ignition direct-connection "Ask MIRA"** (`mira-pipeline/ignition_chat.py`) — the HMI deployment surface. The prompt now carries `Assessment: <one-liner>` (e.g. *"VFD looks healthy (comms OK, no fault) but the machine is stopped — most likely a command/permissive/interlock, not the drive"* or *"Active VFD fault: CE10 modbus timeout…"*) plus the live/asset-context/inference/next-checks separation instruction, alongside the existing `[LIVE TAGS]` block.
- **Why it's not a copy-paste of #2478:** the Ignition wire snapshot (`ignition/webdev/FactoryLM/api/chat/doPost.py`) is `{full_path: {"value": str(qv.value), …}}` — **string values, full-path keys, and ambiguous analog scaling** (raw register vs engineering). Re-scaling an already-engineering value would report a 10×/100×-wrong number. So the new pure helper `live_snapshot.assess_from_paths()` assesses from **only the scaling-immune enum/bool signals** (`vfd_fault_code`, `vfd_comm_ok`, `vfd_cmd_word`, `vfd_status_word`, safety bools) — coercing the string wire value per-leaf-type (so `"False"` isn't treated as truthy) — and **never re-interprets analog values** (they're shown in the preamble, not assessed). Returns `None` (honest silence) when nothing assessable is present; never fabricates.
- **Scope / safety:** text-preamble only; the direct-connection UNS certification, the reject-on-missing-identifier contract, and the trace-only `tag_evidence` are untouched. No engine evidence/citation-contract change, no write path. Defensive import — degrades to no assessment if `shared/` isn't mounted (default behavior preserved).
- **Deferred (documented):** an **analog** assessment on the Ignition path needs a trustworthy value contract (`tag_entities.expected_envelope`, or a raw-vs-engineering wire flag). See `docs/discovery/ignition_live_evidence.md`.
- **Tests:** +8 (`assess_from_paths` over the Ignition wire form incl. healthy-but-stopped / active-fault / `"False"`-not-truthy / analog-only→None / bare-scalar; 2 endpoint tests that the assessment + separation reach the prompt). ### v3.61.7 (2026-07-04) - fix(web): durable Stripe->Hub provisioning with retry + idempotency
- The webhook's `hub_users` bridge was best-effort: if a customer paid before registering on the Hub (`activateHubUserByEmail` UPDATE matched 0 rows) or the Hub DB call threw, the paying customer stayed unprovisioned with no retry. Adds `plg_pending_hub_provisioning` (keyed on the Stripe event id — `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` makes event redelivery a no-op, and the underlying `hub_users` UPDATE is itself idempotent, so replays can never double-provision). The webhook (`checkout.session.completed` / `customer.subscription.deleted`) queues a pending record on `matched=0` or error, and closes queued records once a delivery lands. `reconcilePendingHubProvisioning()` retries pending rows; hooked fire-and-forget into `/api/magic/login` and the `/api/register` returning-active path, and exposed as a `POST` endpoint.
- Verified: 9/9 new tests (`hub-provisioning-queue.test.ts`) pass; `bun test` shows 299 pass / 16 fail / 7 errors — the 16 fail + 7 errors are pre-existing on `main` (identical count, an unrelated `@neondatabase/serverless` dep issue), confirmed by running the same suite against a clean `origin/main` checkout. `bunx tsc --noEmit` shows 35 errors on both this branch and clean `main` (identical pre-existing `"user"` key overload class) — no new type errors introduced.

### v3.60.3 (2026-07-04) - perf(relay): one Neon connection per ingest_batch — cut the ~2s live-tag floor
- **Bottleneck:** the Hub live-tag lag bottomed out at a ~2 s floor set by the relay ingest path, not the browser/collector. `NeonTagStore` opened **3 fresh Neon connections + 3 pre-pings per push** — `_engine()` rebuilt the SQLAlchemy engine on every call with `pool_pre_ping=True`, and `ingest_batch` called `load_allowlist` + `current_state_simulated` + `persist_batch` as three separate connections.
- **Fix:** cache the engine at module level keyed by `neon_url` (`relay_server` builds a fresh `NeonTagStore` per request, so instance caching wouldn't persist); drop `pool_pre_ping` (pure overhead with `NullPool` + Neon's PgBouncer — every `connect()` is already a fresh physical connection); and add `NeonTagStore.session(tenant_id)`, a context manager that opens ONE transaction, runs `SET LOCAL` once, and binds all three pipeline ops to it via `_BoundNeonTagStore`. `ingest_batch` uses the session when the store provides one, else falls back to `nullcontext(store)` so the in-memory test double is unchanged.
- Preserves `persist_batch`'s one-transaction guarantee (strengthened — reads + writes now share the same txn, so any failure rolls the whole push back), keeps the canonical `live_signal_cache` upsert SQL and RLS tenant bind, and stays inside the Contract-5-allowlisted file (one-pipeline law intact).
- Expected push ~2.47 s → ~0.6–0.8 s; with the live SSE push (#2463), 750 ms poll (#2460), and 500 ms Fixed-Delay timer (#2462), sub-second end-to-end. Deploy via `deploy-vps.yml services="mira-relay"`; re-measure with the cadence probe (#2473).
- Verified: 191 relay tests pass (+2 new one-session-per-push regressions), `tests/test_architecture.py` Contract 5 green, `ruff` clean.

### v3.60.2 (2026-07-04) - fix(hub): primary buttons (and controls) invisible in light mode — Tailwind v4 CSS-var syntax
- **Bug:** in **light mode**, the WO-wizard "Next" button (and other primary buttons/controls) were invisible — white text on a white background. They rendered fine in dark mode. Root cause: mira-hub is on **Tailwind v4**, but the shadcn UI components still used the **v3** CSS-variable shorthand `bg-[--brand-blue]`. v4 removed that shorthand (it now requires `bg-[var(--brand-blue)]` or `bg-(--brand-blue)`), so those utilities emitted **no `background-color`** — leaving `text-white` elements that only show against a dark page. The repo was already mid-migration (31 call sites correctly used `bg-[var(--…)]`); the shared components were missed.
- **Fix:** convert the broken `X-[--token]` arbitrary values to the v4-valid `X-[var(--token)]` across the shared UI components (`button`, `select`, `tabs`, `input`, `badge`, `card`) and the demo conveyor page — 55 occurrences, 7 files. Pure syntax migration; no token values or hardcoded hex changed (`.claude/rules/ui-style.md`). Fixes every primary button, dropdown, tab, input, badge, and card in light mode across the hub.
- Verified: transformation is mechanical and structurally clean (no double-wrapped `var(var(`); the correct form matches the 31 pre-existing `[var(--…)]` usages and Tailwind's documented v3→v4 CSS-var change. Live light-mode render validated by CI build + post-deploy.

### v3.60.1 (2026-07-04) - perf(hub): SSE push for the Machine Memory live-signal card (Tier 2)
- Closes stage 5 of `docs/perf/live-latency-budget.md` (the browser poll) — the Machine Memory card now holds an `EventSource` connection to a new `GET /api/assets/[id]/machine-memory/stream` route instead of polling every 750 ms. The route re-assembles the same response every 350 ms and pushes the full payload the instant `live_tags`/`current_state` changes (or every 3 s regardless, so runs/windows/anomalies still refresh). Each tick opens+releases its own pooled `withTenantContext` connection — never held across ticks — and a transient DB error just skips that tick instead of killing the stream. 15 s heartbeat comments keep proxies from dropping the connection; a 10-minute lifetime cap forces a clean reconnect. The card falls back to its existing polling `setInterval` if the SSE connection errors (e.g. a proxy blocking `text/event-stream`), so a blocked stream never breaks the card.
- Extracts the GET route's response assembly (uns_path resolve → `fetchMachineMemory`/`fetchLiveSignals` → freshness classification → `deriveCurrentState` → `formatTagValue`) into `mira-hub/src/lib/machine-memory-response.ts` (`buildMachineMemoryResponse`), reused byte-for-byte by both the polling GET route and the new SSE route. `MachineMemoryCard.tsx`'s `MachineMemoryResponse` type now re-exports from that single source; its success-branch handling (change-flash detection + `changeCounts`) is extracted into a shared `applyData()` used by both the initial GET and every SSE message.

### v3.59.5 (2026-07-04) - perf(ignition): collector timer 2000ms Fixed-Rate -> 500ms Fixed-Delay
- The FactoryLM collector's gateway timer (`MiraTagStream/resource.json`) pushed one tag batch every 2000 ms (Fixed Rate) — the single biggest controllable stage in the tag->Hub latency budget (`docs/perf/live-latency-budget.md`). Now `delay: 500, fixedDelay: true` (Fixed Delay): waits 500 ms after each push completes, so a slow cloud POST can never overlap/pile up, and cache freshness improves ~2 s -> ~0.7 s. **Applies only after an Ignition service restart** (config-as-files is not hot-reloaded) — a bench deploy step, not automatic.

### v3.59.4 (2026-07-04) - perf(hub): faster live-tag display poll + latency budget doc
- Live-tag latency was ~3.5 s typical / ~7 s worst because the pipeline stacks **three independent polls** (gateway scan ~1 s + collector push 2 s + browser poll 2 s), each adding up to its full interval. Documents the full per-layer budget in `docs/perf/live-latency-budget.md` and drops the card display poll (`MachineMemoryCard.tsx POLL_INTERVAL_MS`) from 2000 → 750 ms so the browser stays ahead of a faster collector. The dominant levers (collector timer 2000→500 ms, a 250 ms gateway scan class) are gateway settings; sub-second "instant" is the Tier-2 SSE-push follow-up (the relay already has a WebSocket).

### v3.59.3 (2026-07-04) - fix(historian): cross-window cooldown for info-severity anomalies (#2431)
- A persistent MEDIUM/LOW/INFO condition (e.g. A9 out-of-range DC bus) re-fired one identical `run_diff` row per state-transition window. New `RunStore.recent_anomaly_pair_ts()` + `historize_machine_memory(anomaly_cooldown_seconds=1800)` suppress an info-severity anomaly when the same `(diff_type, tag_path)` was written within the cooldown, regardless of window; CRITICAL/HIGH keep their per-window row. Worker knob `MIRA_ANOMALY_COOLDOWN_SECONDS` (0 disables); summary gains `anomalies_cooldown_suppressed`. 4 new tests.

### v3.59.0 (2026-07-04) - feat(wiring-diagram): grounded IEC-60617 electrical-print generator
- Adds `mira-bots/shared/wiring_diagram/` — a spec-driven electrical wiring-diagram generator (schema → symbols → layout → renderer). Consumes a validated `DiagramSpec` (components + terminals + connections + buses) and renders **SVG** (dependency-free), **PNG/PDF** (via PyMuPDF/`fitz`, imported lazily). No LLM call lives in the renderer — provider-agnostic (PRD §4). **Provenance:** lifted from `openclaw/openclaw/diagram/` (MIT, FactoryLM) per `docs/discovery/electrical_print_reuse_audit.md`; the PNG path was switched off cairosvg (LGPL) to `fitz` and a vector `render_pdf` added. openclaw shipped the engine with **no tests**; this adds `mira-bots/tests/test_wiring_diagram.py` (7 tests: IR round-trip, SVG carries components/terminals/wires, PNG/PDF magic-byte checks — `pytest.importorskip("fitz")` so the bot-test CI env skips the render cases while the SVG core always runs — a cairosvg-absence license guard, markdown summary).
- Adds the **grounded** CV-101 worked example under `docs/onboarding/cv-101-evidence/`: `build_cv101_print.py` constructs the `DiagramSpec` **strictly from cited bench evidence** (`wiring_evidence.md`) — confirmed devices + connections only; UNKNOWN loads/terminals/wiring are recorded as explicit gap NOTES rather than invented — and emits `cv101_print.{svg,pdf}` + `cv101_diagram_spec.json`.
- **Scope note:** self-contained library + grounded demo; not yet wired into a production bot/MCP/HMI surface. `fitz` (PyMuPDF) is AGPL-3.0 — already present on `main` (email adapter, `plc/conv_simple_electrical/render_sheet.py`), so this introduces no new licensing posture, but flag it for any customer-shipped path.

### v3.58.12 (2026-07-04) - feat(crew): dogfood autonomous filing + RED escalation (durability Phase 4)

Safe by construction: a RED is filed only after a *second* persona reproduces it, deduped first, and on a dedupe match in non-interactive mode `create_issue.sh` **declines silently** (no re-file, no repeat comment), so a persistent RED files exactly once. ### v3.58.3 (2026-07-03) - fix(ignition): guard `__file__` in tag allowlist/collector for Jython script-resource scope
- On a real Ignition gateway, `allowlist.py` and `collector.py` run as **project script-library resources**, where Jython does **not** define `__file__`. Both modules dereferenced `os.path.abspath(__file__)` at **import time** (allowlist for its in-repo fallback path; collector for the `api/chat` `sys.path` insert), so importing either as a script resource raised `NameError: name '__file__' is not defined` — breaking tag-allowlist resolution on the exact deployment surface the Maintenance-Intelligence panel uses (WebDev module not installed → Perspective project-library scripts). Both now guard the `__file__` use in `try/except NameError`, falling back to the absolute Gateway install paths (allowlist) / flat-sibling import (collector). Also adds the non-`projects/` `data/factorylm/approved_tags.json` install-path variants. Verified: main raises `NameError` on a no-`__file__` import; the guarded version imports and resolves cleanly. 51 ignition tests green (`tests/ignition/test_allowlist.py`, `test_tag_collector.py`, `tests/test_conveyor_allowlist_parity.py`).

These suites are the only thing that keeps the **verify-before-file gate** honest (independent reproduction + distinct verifier + dedupe); before this they ran in NO CI, so the gate could silently regress into filing false bugs. ### v3.55.4 (2026-07-03) - feat(crew): beta-gate dogfood journey + fix(hub): QA seeder tenants mirror
- Adds the **beta-gate** human journey to the dogfood judge (`tools/crew/dogfood/checks/beta-gate.check`): as an owner persona, create a namespace node → **upload a manual through the real folder=brain door** (`/api/namespace/node/<id>/files/` → real ingest) → wait for ingestion → ask the **node-scoped** chat a question the manual answers. Because node-chat reads only that node's brain, a cited answer PROVES retrieval of the upload — it can't be faked by the shared OEM corpus. This is the daily-deploy-truth companion to the CI release gate (`tests/beta/beta_ready_upload_retrieval_citation.py`). ### v3.55.3 (2026-07-03) - fix(hub): GET /api/assets/[id]/context 404'd for real assets (wrong id-space)
- The UNS confirmation-gate context endpoint looked the `[id]` path param up in **`kg_entities`**, but that param is a **`cmms_equipment.id`** — the canonical asset id-space every other asset sub-route (`detail`/`documents`/`chat`/`validation-qa`) keys on. A CMMS-registered asset that hasn't been promoted to a `kg_entities` row (the common case) therefore returned **404 "Asset not found"** for an asset that plainly exists, breaking the "is this the right asset?" confirmation card. The route now resolves identity from `cmms_equipment` (404 only if truly absent there) and enriches `uns_path` from `kg_entities` via the same `(id::text=$ OR entity_id=$)` bridge the asset-chat route uses — `null` when there's no kg row. (Separate query, not a join: `cmms_equipment.tenant_id` is TEXT but `kg_entities.tenant_id` is UUID, so a column compare errors.) Found by the dogfood judge's contextualization path (`/context` 404 despite the asset existing); verified live against staging (query returns the asset) + 3 regression tests (`context/__tests__/route.test.ts`). Hub release `mira-hub/v2.24.2`.

### v3.53.4 (2026-07-01) - feat(crew): synthetic-worker runner + dogfood judge + retries/--until-find
> Note: `v3.53.3` was independently taken by #2387 on main; this crew PR ships as `v3.53.4`, so the runner + judge (originally staged as 3.53.3) is released here together with the retries / `--until-find` work.
- Adds `tools/crew/dogfood/judge.sh` + four `.check` packs (maintenance-tech, contextualization, work-order, demo-readiness) that walk MIRA's core product paths against the live staging Hub as real QA personas and classify each GREEN/YELLOW/RED in **business language**, writing a two-minute founder report to `qa/dogfood/latest-report.md`. Every RED is cross-verified under a **second** persona session before it can be filed (finder≠verifier), deduped first, refused on INFRA/ambiguous; deterministic corpus-aware asset selection avoids flaky verdicts.
- Adds the gated filer `tools/qa/create_issue.sh` + `tools/crew/run_synthetic_workers.sh`: no finding is filed without an independent reproduction, a distinct verifier, `dogfood`/`crew` labels, and (for P0) `--allow-p0`. Dry-run by default; no app/runtime code.
- The synthetic-worker runner now persists across transient blips and keeps probing until it finds a real bug — **without lowering the verify-before-file gate**. `--retries N` (default 3, `--retry-delay`) treats a scenario as reproduced if the bug signal appears on ANY attempt (defeats network/deploy-not-landed flakiness, catches intermittent bugs); "reproduced" still means the deterministic bug signal was observed.
- `--until-find` (+ `--max-rounds`/`--max-seconds` budget) re-runs ALL scenarios in rounds until one reproduces a real, gate-passing bug OR the budget is hit. A healthy system stops honestly at the budget with `found=0` ("nothing to fix") — it never invents a finding to satisfy the flag. Per-round artifacts land in `<out>/round-N/`.
- Adds two false-positive-resistant probe scenarios so `--until-find` has real invariants to test: `wo-roundtrip` (create-time work-order priority/title must survive a re-read — #2375-class) and `asset-detail-parity` (a listed asset must be fetchable by id, read-only consistency). Both emit a bug signal ONLY on an unambiguous HTTP-200-but-wrong-data violation; any non-200 is treated as transient and refused, so HTTP flakiness is never filed as a bug. Hermetic tests — judge 10/10, runner **19/19** (12 original + 7 new), gate 7/7; shellcheck clean. Verified live against staging: retries visible, honest budget-exhaust, no manufactured finding.

### v3.53.2 (2026-06-30) - fix(hub): GET /api/work-orders/[id] returns resolution + closed_at (#2375)
- A completed work order read back with `resolution=null` and `closed_at=null` even though PATCH persisted them — the GET detail `SELECT` and `rowToWO` serializer omitted the closure columns, so the next technician saw a blank closure. The GET now selects and returns `resolution`, `fault_description`, and `closed_at`.
- Found by the dogfood judge (`tools/crew/dogfood`) and reproduced field-by-field against staging (PATCH returns the values; GET dropped the keys entirely). Regression test `mira-hub/src/app/api/work-orders/[id]/route.test.ts`. Hub release `mira-hub/v2.24.1`.

### v3.39.17 (2026-06-22) — test(eval): skip non-deterministic FSM check on vfd_danfoss_04 out-of-KB fixture
- **Problem:** `vfd_danfoss_04_vlt_fc360_edge` (user asks about a nonexistent VLT FC 360) is a stochastic out-of-KB edge case. The engine's `Q→DIAGNOSIS` gate transition is LLM-non-deterministic, so the terminal FSM state flips `Q1`/`Q2`/`DIAGNOSIS` run-to-run; the grader's `cp_reached_state` then fails whenever it lands at `Q1` — producing **11/11 spurious FSM-only failures** in the #1948 eval-flakiness triage even though keyword + citation checks pass.
- **Fix:** added `skip_fsm_check: true` (the grader's purpose-built flag for exactly this class — `tests/eval/grader.py:110`), so the fixture validates honest out-of-KB behavior via `expected_keywords` + citation groundedness instead of FSM depth. Mirrors the existing `04_yaskawa_out_of_kb.yaml` precedent. Fixture-only; no engine/grader code change.
- **Context:** follow-up **(c)** from the #1948 triage (PR #2222). Siblings: #2258 (eval-suite determinism via record/replay), #2257 (Nemotron-404 reranker outage). PR #2256.

### v3.39.14 (2026-06-22) — docs+tools(kb): full-PDF docling ingest tooling + don't-promote findings
- **Outcome:** bulk-loading full OEM manuals into the shared corpus is NOT the lever for answer quality (retrieval ranking is — #2237). `docling` extraction works (772 Micro820 tables → Markdown; quality gate drops `�`/`CCChhh` noise), but staging retrieval showed full-manual chunks don't surface better than the curated chunks already covering GS10/Micro820. Loaded chunks deleted from staging; **nothing to prod.**
- **Delivered (docs + tools only, no engine/service code):** `ingest_local_pdf.py` (`--use-docling` + quality gate), `verify_seed.py` / `retrieval_check.py` / `coverage_check.py`, the shared-corpus load runbook (`docs/runbooks/load-oem-manuals-into-kb.md`), and the plan + verdict (`docs/plans/2026-06-22-full-pdf-docling-ingest-plan.md`). Ready to re-run if/when the page-picking work lands. PR #2238.

### v3.39.13 (2026-06-22) — feat(retrieval): equipment-aware reranking in production (behind flag)
- **Problem (verified on the prod path, not the harness):** `recall_knowledge` RRF is vendor-blind — "GS10 overcurrent" ranked a Yaskawa **V1000** chunk #1 over GS10. The equipment-scope rerank that fixes it lived **only** in `tests/mira_bench.py`, so every live surface (Telegram/Slack/pipeline/Hub) shipped vendor-confused retrieval.
- **Fix:** ported an equipment rerank into `mira-bots/shared/neon_recall.py`, **behind `MIRA_EQUIPMENT_RERANK` (default OFF → zero prod impact until Phase 4)**. Overfetch → RRF → float chunks matching the query's extracted equipment → truncate. Positive-boost only (no harness `v1000/powerflex` denylist, so a real V1000/PowerFlex question still returns that vendor); no equipment in query ⇒ no-op.
- **Evidence:** unit `tests/regime2_rag/test_equipment_rerank.py` 5/5; raw prod path on staging — vendor confusion eliminated; retrieval A/B (`tools/seeds/oem-manuals/phase3_retrieval_ab.py`) avg relevance **0.62 → 0.96**, coverage 0.75 → 1.00, **0/10 regressions**. ### v3.39.10 (2026-06-22) — fix(ci): Hub E2E required check no longer blocks docs/non-hub PRs
- **Bug:** `hub-e2e.yml` (the required status check "Hub E2E (command-center + onboarding)") used an `on:`-level `paths-ignore` (`docs/**`, `wiki/**`, `**/*.md`, `.claude/**`). A required check suppressed by a path filter **never reports its context**, so any all-ignored PR (e.g. docs-only #2199) sat `Expected` → permanently `BLOCKED` and could only land via admin-merge.
- **Fix:** removed the `on:`-level `paths-ignore`. The workflow now always runs on PRs to main and reports the required context; cost stays controlled **inside the job** by the existing `dorny/paths-filter` `changes` step + `if: steps.changes.outputs.hub == 'true'` gates, which short-circuit non-hub PRs to trivially-green in seconds (the workflow's own documented design). No change to what e2e actually runs on hub PRs.

Governance + incident checks run observationally under `MIRA_TRACE_CHECKS=1`. JSON-first, read-only, **off by default = zero prod behavior change**. SimLab eval-pack runner + CLI viewer.

Observational output-contract check.

### v3.36.0 (2026-06-21) — feat(pipeline): asset-agent deployment gate resolver (Northstar Phase 4)
- Makes the train-before-deploy gate **functional**. `mira-pipeline/ignition_chat.py` `_lookup_agent_state()` was a self-described **NON-FUNCTIONAL** stub — it matched the incoming Ignition token *literally* against `asset_agent_status.uns_path::text`/`equipment_id::text`, but the token is a tag-path (`[default]Conv/State`) or display name that never equals a stored ltree/UUID → refuse-all when `ENFORCE_ASSET_AGENT_GATE` is on.
- **Real resolution** (new `_agent_state_from_conn` seam + local `_slug`): JOINs the bridge tables so a structured `asset_context`/display-name token resolves via `cmms_equipment.equipment_number` (slug-normalized, e.g. `GS10-VFD`→`gs10_vfd`) — the robust path, independent of the nullable `cmms_equipment.uns_path` backfill — plus the canonical `uns_path`/`equipment_id` forms and best-effort Ignition tag-path via `installed_component_instances.plc_tag`. Tenant-isolated by the driving `asset_agent_status.tenant_id` predicate (JOINs key on the tenant-owned `equipment_id` UUID); no migration.
- **Residual gap (documented, default-OFF preserved):** a flat Ignition tag-path only resolves when `plc_tag` is populated (e.g. by the tag-CSV import); absent that, such turns refuse. Keep `ENFORCE_ASSET_AGENT_GATE` OFF until proven per tenant.
- Doctrine: `mira-uns-architecture` (local `_slug` mirrors `uns.slug()`; mira-pipeline can't import mira-crawler), `train-before-deploy`, `direct-connection-uns-certified`. Read-only; gate decision/answer branch + 422 `uns_required` untouched; hallucination-audit clean for the diff.
- Tests: `mira-pipeline/tests/test_ignition_chat_resolver.py` (+8: slug grammar, param binding, query covers all forms, miss→None, state passthrough). Gate + direct-connection suites unchanged-green (20). NOTE: a pre-existing `direct_connection`→`gate` test-ordering pollution (7 fails) reproduces on `main` with this change stashed — not introduced here.

### v3.33.3 (2026-06-21) — fix(plc-parser): bundle tag_csv.py into mira-ingest image (CSV uploads 500'd)
- **Follow-up to v3.33.2.** Wiring `mira_plc_parser` into the mira-ingest image (v3.33.2) exposed a latent gap: the CSV parser (`mira_plc_parser/parsers/csv_tags.py`) reuses the pure `tag_csv.py` from the Ignition tree by *path* (`parents[3]/ignition/webdev/FactoryLM/api/diagnose/tag_csv.py`). The image COPYs only the package, so that path is absent in-container → CSV uploads to `/ingest/plc-parse` returned **500 (`FileNotFoundError`)**. Verified live on prod after the v3.33.2 deploy (L5X 200 ✓, CSV 500 ✗). Not a regression — CSV was unreachable (503/stuck) before; now it parses.
- **`csv_tags.py`** — `_load_tag_csv()` now honors `MIRA_TAG_CSV_PATH` (explicit override for packaged deployments) before the repo-layout default, and raises an actionable error if neither resolves. Backward-compatible: dev / CLI / the parser's own tests (where the repo tree exists) are unchanged.
- **`mira-core/mira-ingest/Dockerfile`** — bundles `ignition/…/tag_csv.py` → `/app/vendor/tag_csv.py` and sets `ENV MIRA_TAG_CSV_PATH`. The file is pure/self-contained (no further sideloads), so no other change is needed.
- Why CI missed it: the parser's tests run in the repo layout (where the path resolves) and aren't in CI; the Docker Build Check builds but doesn't exercise `/ingest/plc-parse`. New `tests/test_csv_tags_path.py` (+5) guards the env-override resolution + the missing-path error. Golden CSV test unchanged (4).

### v3.33.2 (2026-06-21) — fix(contextualization): replace dead Python parse worker with inline mira-ingest HTTP call
- **P0: in-Hub PLC upload worker was dead on prod.** The contextualization sources route spawned `python ctx_parse_worker.py <id>`, but the Hub ships as a Node-alpine image (build context `./mira-hub`) with no Python, no `psycopg2`, and no `mira_plc_parser` on it. `spawn()` emits an async `'error'` rather than throwing, so the route returned `workerStarted:true` while the child died — every `ctx_sources` row stuck at `status='pending'`.
- **`mira-hub/src/lib/contextualization/parse-source.ts`** (new) — `parsePlcViaIngest()` forwards the upload to mira-ingest `/ingest/plc-parse` (reusing the `lib/plc-import.ts` pattern); `reportToExtractions()` ports the worker's tag-dictionary → `ctx_extractions` mapping. **`…/[id]/sources/route.ts`** — removed the spawn; parse inline over HTTP, write extractions, flip to `done`. **Every** parse failure (422/413/503/502/timeout/DB-write) flips the source to `error` + `error_message` — never stuck `pending`. UI consumes the terminal status. Dead worker + test deleted.
- **mira-ingest image** — wired the stdlib-only `mira_plc_parser` package in (repo-root build context + COPY) so `/ingest/plc-parse` returns 200 instead of 503. Updated **all** ingest build sites to repo-root context: `docker-compose.saas.yml`, `mira-core/docker-compose.yml` (dev/oracle), `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (Docker Build Check). Added a repo-root `.dockerignore` so root-context builds stop shipping node_modules/.git/.next. Also added `relevance.py` to the ingest COPY allow-list (imported by `main.py`, previously omitted; harmless only because `RELEVANCE_GATE_ENABLED` defaults off).
- Scope: restores **PLC-export (L5X / vendor tag CSV) parity** — the inputs the dead worker handled. PDF/manual content extraction is unchanged (still 422s → `error`); a separate gap.
- Tests: 83/83 contextualization+plc unit tests (5 new mapper tests). Local `docker build` of mira-ingest from repo root verified green.

### v3.33.0 (2026-06-20) — feat(hub): materialize tag_entities on PLC tag_mapping accept (Phase 8)
- Closes the last functional gap in the offline **PLC Parser → Hub tag-import** chain (Northstar plan Phase 8): approving a parser-proposed `tag_mapping` in `/proposals` now creates a **verified `tag_entities` row** (mig 025), so an approved PLC tag becomes a typed, queryable signal the relay / engine / MCP read — not just a flipped status. Previously `tag_mapping` accept was status-only (only `kg_entity` materialized an entity).
- **`mira-hub/src/lib/suggestion-accept.ts`** — `decideSuggestion` verify path now branches `tag_mapping` → `createTagEntity()`. New exported `mapTagDataType()` maps the parser's *declared* PLC/IEC/Rockwell type (BOOL/DINT/WORD/REAL/…) to the `tag_entities.data_type` CHECK enum; an export with no declarable type (CCW name-only case) is transitioned but **not** materialized — the typed table never holds an invented type. Insert is `approval_state='verified'`, `proposed_by='import:plc_parser'`, idempotent via `ON CONFLICT (tenant_id, uns_path)`.
- Verified vs proposed honored: materialization happens only on the explicit human accept (plc-tag-mapper rule — never auto-verify). Read-only; no PLC writes.
- Tests: `suggestion-accept.test.ts` +6 cases (typed materialization, name-only/unmappable skip, reject, `mapTagDataType`). Full file green (12); adjacent `plc-proposals` suite unchanged (7).
